7.4|Refraction|137
In the previous sections we studied Light Reflection (physics) off various surfaces. What happens when Light passes through medium? Like all Wave the Speed of Light is dependent on the medium in which it is travelling. When Light moves from one medium into another (for example from air to glass) the Speed of Light changes. The effect is that the Light Ray (optics) passing into new medium is Refraction or bent. Refraction is therefore the bending of Light as it moves from one Geometrical optics medium to another. Definition: Refraction Refraction is the bending of Light that occurs because Light travels at different Speed in different materials. When Light travels from one medium to another it will be bent away from its original path. When it travels from an Geometrical optics dense medium like water or glass to less dense medium like air it will be Refraction away from the normal (Figure 7.9). Whereas if it travels from less dense medium to denser one it will be Refraction towards the normal (Figure 7.10). Just as we defined an angle of Reflection (physics) in the previous section we can similarly define an angle of Refraction as the angle between the surface normal and the Refraction Ray (optics) This is shown in Figure 7.11. Figure 7.9: Light is moving from an Geometrical optics dense medium to an Geometrical optics less dense medium. Light is Refraction away from the normal. Figure 7.10: Light is moving from an Geometrical optics less dense medium to an Geometrical optics denser medium. Light is Refraction towards the normal. Figure 7.11: Light moving from one medium to another bends towards or away from the surface normal. The angle of Refraction is shown. 
---------------------------------------------------------

7.4.1|Refractive Index|139
Which is easier to travel through air or water? People usually travel faster through air. So does Light The Speed of Light and therefore the degree of bending of the Light depends on the Refraction index of material through which the Light passes. The Refraction index (symbol n) is the ratio of the Speed of Light in vacuum to its Speed in the material. You can think of the Refraction index as measure of how difficult it is for Light to get through material. Definition: Refraction Index The Refraction index of material is the ratio of the Speed of Light in vacuum to its Speed in the medium. The symbol is used to represent the Speed of Light in vacuum. 299 792 485m s1 For purposes of calculation we use 108m s1. vacuum is region with no matter in it not even air. However the Speed of Light in air is very close to that in vacuum. Definition: Refraction Index The Refraction index (symbol n) of material is the ratio of the Speed of Light in vacuum to its Speed in the material and gives an indication of how difficult it is for Light to get through the material. where Refraction index (no unit) Speed of Light in vacuum (300 108m s1) Speed of Light in given medium (m s1) Extension: Refraction Index and Speed of Light Using we can also examine how the Speed of Light changes in different media because the Speed of Light in vacuum (c) is constant. If the Refraction index increases the Speed of Light in the material must decrease. Light therefore travels slowly through materials of high n. Table 7.4.1 shows Refraction indices for various materials. Light travels slower in any material than it does in vacuum so all values for are greater than 1. 
---------------------------------------------------------

7.4.2|Snell's Law|139
Now that we know that the degree of bending or the angle of Refraction is dependent on the Refraction index of medium how do we calculate the angle of Refraction The Angle of incidence and Refraction when Light travels from one medium to another can be calculated using Snell's law Table 7.1: Refraction indices of some materials. nair is calculated at STP and all values are determined for yellow sodium Light which has Wavelength of 5893 nm. Definition: Snell's law n1 sin n2 sin where n1 Refraction index of material n2 Refraction index of material Angle of Angle of incidence of Refraction Remember that Angle of incidence and Refraction are measured from the normal which is an imaginary line perpendicular to the surface. Suppose we have two media with Refraction indices n1 and n2. Light Ray (optics) is incident on the surface between these materials with an Angle of incidence 1. The Refraction Ray (optics) that passes through the second medium will have an angle of Refraction 2. If n2 n1 then from Snell's law sin sin 2. For angles smaller than 90 sin increases as increases. Therefore 2. This means that the Angle of incidence is greater than the angle of Refraction and the Light Ray (optics) is bent toward the normal. Similarly if n2 n1 then from Snell's law sin sin 2. For angles smaller than 90 sin increases as increases. Therefore 2. This means that the Angle of incidence is less than the angle of Refraction and the Light Ray (optics) is away toward the normal. Both these situations can be seen in Figure 7.12. Figure 7.12: Refraction of two Light Ray (optics) (a) Ray (optics) travels from medium of low Refraction index to one of high Refraction index. The Ray (optics) is bent towards the normal. (b) Ray (optics) travels from medium with high Refraction index to one with low Refraction index. The Ray (optics) is bent away from the normal. What happens to Ray (optics) that lies along the normal line? In this case the Angle of incidence is and sin n1 n2 sin 0. This shows that if the Light Ray (optics) is incident at then the angle of Refraction is also 0. The Ray (optics) passes through the surface unchanged i.e. no Refraction occurs. 
---------------------------------------------------------

Imagine coin on the bottom of shallow pool of water. If you reach for the coin you will miss it because the Light Ray (optics) from the coin are Refraction at the waters surface. Consider Light Ray (optics) that travels from an underwater object to your eye. The Ray (optics) is Refraction at the water surface and then reaches your eye. Your eye does not know Snell's law it assumes Light Ray (optics) travel in straight lines. Your eye therefore sees the image of the at coin shallower location. This shallower location is known as the apparent depth. The Refraction index of medium can also be expressed as

7.5|Mirrors|146
mirror is highly Reflection (physics) surface. The most common mirrors are flat and are known as Plane mirror Household mirrors are Plane mirror They are made of flat piece of glass with thin layer of silver nitrate or aluminium on the back. However other mirrors are curved and are either Curved mirror or are Curved mirror The Reflection (physics) properties of all three types of mirrors will be discussed in this section. 
---------------------------------------------------------

7.5.1|Image Formation|146
Definition: Image An image is representation of an object formed by mirror or lens. Light from the image is seen. If you place candle in front of mirror you now see two candles. The actual Physics candle is called the object and the picture you see in the mirror is called the image. The object is the source of the incident Ray (optics) The image is the picture that is formed by the Reflection (physics) Ray (optics) The object could be an actual source that emits Light such as Light bulb or candle. More commonly the object Reflection (physics) Light from another source. When you look at your face in the mirror your face does not emit Light Instead Light from Light bulb or from the sun Reflection (physics) off your face and then hits the mirror. However in Work (physics) with Light Ray (optics) it is easiest to pretend the Light is coming from the object. An image formed by Reflection (physics) may be real or virtual. Real image occurs when Light Ray (optics) actually intersect at the image. Real image is inverted or upside down. Virtual image occurs when Light Ray (optics) do not actually meet at the image. Instead you see the image because your eye projects Light Ray (optics) backward. You are fooled into seeing an image Virtual image is erect or right side up (upright). You can tell the two types apart by putting screen at the location of the image. Real image can be formed on the screen because the Light Ray (optics) actually meet there. Virtual image cannot be seen on screen since it is not really there. To describe objects and images we need to know their locations and their sizes. The Distance from the mirror to the object is the object Distance do. The Distance from the mirror to the image is the image Distance di. 
---------------------------------------------------------

7.5.2|Plane Mirrors|147
When you look into mirror you see an image of yourself. The image created in the mirror has the following properties: 1. The image is virtual. 2. The image is the same Distance behind the mirror as the object is in front of the mirror. 3. The image is laterally inverted. This means that the image is inverted from side to side. 4. The image is the same size as the object. 5. The image is upright. Virtual image are images formed in places where Light does not really reach. Light does not really pass through the mirror to create the image it only appears to an observer as though the Light were coming from behind the mirror. Whenever mirror creates an image which is virtual the image will always be located behind the mirror where Light does not really pass. Definition: Virtual image Virtual image is upright on the opposite side of the mirror as the object and Light does not actually reach it. 
---------------------------------------------------------

7.5.3|Ray Diagrams|148
We draw Ray (optics) diagrams to predict the image that is formed by Plane mirror Ray (optics) diagram is geometrical picture that is used for analyzing the images formed by mirrors and lenses. We draw few characteristic Ray (optics) from the object to the mirror. We then follow ray-tracing rules to find the path of the Ray (optics) and locate the image. Important: mirror obeys Specular reflection The Ray (optics) diagram for the image formed by Plane mirror is the simplest possible Ray (optics) diagram. Figure 7.15 shows an object placed in front of Plane mirror It is convenient to have central line that runs perpendicular to the mirror. This imaginary line is called the principal axis. Important: Ray (optics) diagrams The following should be remembered when drawing Ray (optics) diagrams: 1. Objects are represented by arrows. The Length of the arrow represents the height of the object. 2. If the arrow points upwards then the object is described as upright or erect. If the arrow points downwards then the object is described as inverted. 3. If the object is real then the arrow is drawn with solid line. If the object is virtual then the arrow is drawn with dashed line. Method: Ray (optics) Diagrams for Plane mirror Ray (optics) diagrams are used to find the Position (vector) and size and whether the image is real or virtual. 1. Draw the Plane mirror as straight line on principal axis. 2. Draw the object as an arrow in front of the mirror. 3. Draw the image of the object by using the principle that the image is placed at the same Distance behind the mirror that the object is in front of the mirror. The image size is also the same as the object size. 4. Place dot at the point the eye is located. 5. Pick one point on the image and draw the Reflection (physics) Ray (optics) that travels to the eye as it sees this point. Remember to add an arrowhead. 6. Draw the incident Ray (optics) for Light traveling from the corresponding point on the object to the mirror such that Specular reflection is obeyed. 7. Continue for other extreme points on the object. Suppose Light Ray (optics) leaves the top of the object traveling parallel to the principal axis. The Ray (optics) will hit the mirror at an Angle of incidence of degrees. We say that the Ray (optics) hits the mirror normally. According to Specular reflection the Ray (optics) will be Reflection (physics) at degrees. The Ray (optics) then bounces back in the same Direction (geometry) We also project the Ray (optics) back behind the mirror because this is what your eye does. Another Light Ray (optics) leaves the top of the object and hits the mirror at its centre. This Ray (optics) will be Reflection (physics) at the same angle as its Angle of incidence as shown. If we project the Ray (optics) backward behind the mirror it will eventually cross the projection of the first Ray (optics) we drew. We have found the location of the image It is Virtual image since it appears in an area that Light cannot actually reach (behind the mirror). You can see from the diagram that the image is erect and is the same size as the object. This is exactly as we expected. We use dashed line to indicate that the image is virtual. 
---------------------------------------------------------

7.5.4|Spherical Mirrors|150

These two mirrors will be studied in detail. The centre of curvature is the point at the centre of the sphere and describes how big the sphere is.

7.5.5|Concave Mirrors|150
The first type of Curved mirror we will study are Curved mirror Curved mirror have the shape shown in Figure 7.17. As with Plane mirror the principal axis is line that is perpendicular to the centre of the mirror. If you think of Light Reflection (physics) off Curved mirror you will immediately see that things will look very different compared to Plane mirror The easiest way to understand what will happen is to draw Ray (optics) diagram and Work (physics) out where the images will form. Once we have done that it is easy to see what properties the image has. First we need to define very important characteristic of the mirror. We have seen that the centre of curvature is the centre of the sphere from which the mirror is cut. We then define that Distance that is half-way between the centre of curvature and the mirror on the principal axis. This point is known as the focal point and the Distance from the focal point to the mirror is known as the focal Length (symbol f). Since the focal point is the midpoint of the line segment joining the vertex and the center of curvature the focal Length would be one-half the radius of curvature. This fact can come in very handy remember if you know one then you know the other Definition: Focal Point The focal point of mirror is the midpoint of line segment joining the vertex and the centre of curvature. It is the Position (vector) at which all parallel Ray (optics) are focussed. Why are we making such big deal about this point we call the focal point? It has an important property we will use often. Ray (optics) parallel to the principal axis hitting the mirror will always be Reflection (physics) through the focal point. The focal point is the Position (vector) at which all parallel Ray (optics) are focussed. Figure 7.19: Curved mirror with three Ray (optics) drawn to locate the image. Each incident Ray (optics) is Reflection (physics) according to Specular reflection The intersection of the Reflection (physics) Ray (optics) gives the location of the image. Here the image is real and inverted. From Figure 7.19 we see that the image created by Curved mirror is real and inverted as compared to the virtual and erect image created by Plane mirror Definition: Real image Real image can be cast on screen it is inverted and on the same side of the mirror as the object. 
---------------------------------------------------------

7.5.6|Convex Mirrors|153
The second type of Curved mirror we will study are Curved mirror Curved mirror have the shape shown in Figure 7.20. As with Plane mirror the principal axis is line that is perpendicular to the centre of the mirror. We have defined the focal point as that point that is half-way along the principal axis between the centre of curvature and the mirror. Now for Curved mirror this point is behind the mirror. Curved mirror has negative focal Length because the focal point is behind the mirror. Figure 7.20: Curved mirror with principle axis focal point (F) and centre of curvature (C). The centre of the mirror is the Geometrical optics centre (O). To determine what the image from Curved mirror looks like and where the image is located we need to remember that mirror obeys Specular reflection and that Light appears to come from the image. The image created by Curved mirror is shown in Figure 7.21. Figure 7.21: Curved mirror with three Ray (optics) drawn to locate the image. Each incident Ray (optics) is Reflection (physics) according to Specular reflection The Reflection (physics) Ray (optics) diverge. If the Reflection (physics) Ray (optics) are extended behind the mirror then their intersection gives the location of the image behind the mirror. For Curved mirror the image is virtual and upright. From Figure 7.21 we see that the image created by Curved mirror is virtual and upright as compared to the real and inverted image created by Curved mirror Extension: Divergence Curved mirror is also known as diverging mirror. Light Ray (optics) appear to diverge from the focal point of Curved mirror

7.5.8|Magnification|154
In Figures 7.19 and 7.21 the height of the object and image arrows were different. In any Geometrical optics system where images are formed from objects the ratio of the image height hi to the object height ho is known as the Magnification m. hi ho This is true for the mirror examples we showed above and will also be true for lenses which will be introduced in the next sections. For Plane mirror the height of the image is the same as the height of the object so the Magnification is simply hi ho 1. If the Magnification is greater than the image is larger than the object and is said to be magnified. If the Magnification is less than the image is smaller than the object so the image is said to be diminished. 
---------------------------------------------------------

7.6|Total Internal Reflection and Fibre Optics|156

---------------------------------------------------------

7.6.1|Total Internal Reflection|156
When we increase the Angle of incidence we reach point where the angle of Refraction is 90 and the Refraction Ray (optics) runs along the surface of the medium. This Angle of incidence is called the critical angle. Definition: Critical Angle The critical angle is the Angle of incidence where the angle of Reflection (physics) is 90. The Light must shine from dense to less dense medium. If the Angle of incidence is bigger than this critical angle the Refraction Ray (optics) will not emerge from the medium but will be Reflection (physics) back into the medium. This is called total internal Reflection (physics) Total internal Reflection (physics) takes place when Light shines from an Geometrical optics denser medium to an Geometrical optics less dense medium. the Angle of incidence is greater than the critical angle. Definition: Total Internal Reflection (physics) Total internal Reflection (physics) takes place when Light is Reflection (physics) back into the medium because the Angle of incidence is greater than the critical angle. Each medium has its own unique critical angle. For example the critical angle for glass is 42 and that of water is 488. We can calculate the critical angle for any medium. Calculating the Critical Angle Now we shall learn how to derive the value of the critical angle for two given media. The process is fairly simple and involves just the use of Snell's law that we have already studied. To recap Snell's law states: n1 sin n2 sin where n1 is the Refraction index of material n2 is the Refraction index of material is the Angle of incidence and is the angle of Refraction For total internal Reflection (physics) we know that the Angle of incidence is the critical angle. So c. However we also know that the angle of Refraction at the critical angle is 90. So we have: 90. We can then write Snell's law as: n1 sin n2 sin 90 Solving for gives: n1 sin n2 sin 90 sin n2 n1 (1) sin1 n2 n1 Important: Take care that for total internal Reflection (physics) the incident Ray (optics) is always in the denser medium. 
---------------------------------------------------------

7.6.2|Fibre Optics|161
Total internal Reflection (physics) is Power (physics) tool since it can be used to confine Light One of the most common applications of total internal Reflection (physics) is in fibre Geometrical optics An Geometrical optics fibre is thin transparent fibre usually made of glass or Plasticity (physics) for transmitting Light Geometrical optics fibres are usually thinner than human hair The construction of single Geometrical optics fibre is shown in Figure 7.23. The basic functional structure of an Geometrical optics fibre consists of an outer protective cladding and an inner core through which Light pulses travel. The overall diameter of the fibre is about 125 (125106m) and that of the core is just about 10 (10106m). The mode of operation of the Geometrical optics fibres as mentioned above depends on the phenomenon of total internal Reflection (physics) The difference in Refraction index of the cladding and the core allows total internal Reflection (physics) in the same way as happens at an air-water surface. If Light is incident on cable end with an Angle of incidence greater than the critical angle then the Light will remain trapped inside the glass strand. In this way Light travels very quickly down the Length of the cable. Fibre Geometrical optics in Telecommunications Geometrical optics fibres are most common in telecommunications because information can be transported over long Distance with minimal loss of data. The minimised loss of data gives Geometrical optics fibres an advantage over conventional cables. Data is transmitted from one end of the fibre to another in the form of Laser pulses. single strand is capable of handling over 3000 simultaneous transmissions which is huge improvement over the conventional co-axial cables. Multiple signal transmission is achieved by sending individual Light pulses at slightly different angles. For example if one of the pulses makes 7223 Angle of incidence then separate pulse can be sent at an angle of 7226 The transmitted data is received almost instantaneously at the other end of the cable since the information coded onto the Laser travels at the Speed of Light During transmission over long Distance repeater stations are used to amplify the signal which has weakened somewhat by the time it reaches the station. The amplified signals are then relayed towards their destination and may encounter several other repeater stations on the way. Fibre Geometrical optics in Medicine Geometrical optics fibres are used in medicine in endoscopes. The main part of an endoscope is the Geometrical optics fibre. Light is shone down the Geometrical optics fibre and medical doctor can use the endoscope to look inside patient. Endoscopes are used to examine the inside of patients stomach by inserting the endoscope down the patients throat. Endoscopes allow minimally invasive surgery. This means that person can be diagnosed and treated through small incision. This has advantages over open surgery because endoscopy is quicker and cheaper and the patient recovers more quickly. The alternative is open surgery which is expensive requires more time and is more traumatic for the patient. Endoscopy means to look inside and refers to looking inside the human body for diagnosing medical conditions. 
---------------------------------------------------------

8|Magnetism|167

---------------------------------------------------------

8.1|Introduction|167
Magnet is the Force that Magnet object exerts through its Magnet Field (physics) on another object. The two objects do not have to Physics touch each other for the Force to be exerted. Object feels the Magnet Force from Object because of Object 1s surrounding Magnet Field (physics) Humans have known about Magnet for many thousands of years. For example lodestone is magnetised form of the iron oxide mineral magnetite. It has the property of attracting iron objects. It is referred to in old European and Asian historical records from around 800 BCE in Europe and around 600 BCE in Asia. The root of the English word Magnet is from the Greek word magnes probably from Magnesia in Asia Minor once an important source of lodestone. 
---------------------------------------------------------

8.2|Magnetic fields|167
Magnet Field (physics) is region in space where Magnet or object made of ferromagnetic material will experience non-contact Force Electron moving inside any object have Magnet Field (physics) associated with them. In most materials these Field (physics) point in all Direction (geometry) so the net Magnet Field (physics) is zero. For example in the Plasticity (physics) ball below the Direction (geometry) of the Magnet Field (physics) of the Electron (shown by the arrows) are pointing in different Direction (geometry) and cancel each other out. Therefore the Plasticity (physics) ball is not Magnet and has no Magnet Field (physics) In some materials (e.g. iron) called ferromagnetic materials there are regions called domains where these Magnet Field (physics) line up. All the atoms in each domain group together so that the Magnet Field (physics) from their Electron point the same way. The picture shows piece of an iron needle zoomed in to show the domains with the Electric field lined up inside them. In permanent Magnet many domains are lined up resulting in net Magnet Field (physics) Objects made from ferromagnetic materials can be magnetised for example by rubbing Magnet along the object in one Direction (geometry) This causes the Magnet Field (physics) of most or all of the domains to line up and cause the object to have Magnet Field (physics) and be Magnet Once ferromagnetic object has been magnetised it can stay Magnet without another Magnet being nearby (i.e. without being in another Magnet Field (physics) In the picture below the needle has been magnetised because the Magnet Field (physics) in all the domains are pointing in the same Direction (geometry) 
---------------------------------------------------------

8.3|Permanent magnets|169

---------------------------------------------------------

8.3.1|The poles of permanent magnets|169
Because the domains in permanent Magnet all line up in particular Direction (geometry) the Magnet has pair of opposite poles called north (usually shortened to N) and south (usually shortened to S). Even if the Magnet is cut into tiny pieces each piece will still have both and pole. These poles always occur in pairs. In nature we never find north Magnet pole or south Magnet pole on its own. Magnet Field (physics) are different to gravitational and Electric field In nature Position (vector) and negative Electric charge can be found on their own but you never find just north Magnet pole or south Magnet pole on its own. On the very small scale zooming in to the size of atoms Magnet Field (physics) are caused by moving Electric charge (i.e. the Electric charge Electron 
---------------------------------------------------------

8.3.2|Magnetic attraction and repulsion|169
Like poles of Magnet repel one another whilst unlike poles attract. This means that two poles or two poles will push away from each other while pole and pole will be drawn towards each other. Definition: Attraction and Repulsion Like poles of Magnet repel each other whilst unlike poles attract each other. 
---------------------------------------------------------

8.3.3|Representing magnetic fields|170
Magnet Field (physics) can be represented using Magnet Field (physics) lines. Although the Magnet Field (physics) of permanent Magnet is everywhere surrounding the Magnet (in all dimensions) we draw only some of the Field (physics) lines to represent the Field (physics) (usually only dimensions are shown in drawings). In areas where the Magnet Field (physics) is strong the Field (physics) lines are closer together. Where the Field (physics) is weaker the Field (physics) lines are drawn further apart. The Strength of materials of Magnet Field (physics) is referred to as the Magnet flux Important: 1. Field (physics) lines never cross. 2. Arrows drawn on the Field (physics) lines indicate the Direction (geometry) of the Field (physics) 3. Magnet Field (physics) points from the north to the south pole of Magnet As the activity shows one can map the Magnet Field (physics) of Magnet by placing it underneath piece of paper and sprinkling iron filings on top. The iron filings line themselves up parallel to the Magnet Field (physics) Another tool one can use to find the Direction (geometry) of Magnet Field (physics) is Compass The Compass arrow points in the Direction (geometry) of the Field (physics) As already said opposite poles of Magnet attract each other and bringing them together causes their Magnet Field (physics) lines to converge (come together). Like poles of Magnet repel each other and bringing them together causes their Magnet Field (physics) lines to diverge (bend out from each other). Extension: Ferromagnetism and Retentivity Ferromagnetism is phenomenon shown by materials like iron nickel or cobalt. These materials can form permanent Magnet They always magnetise so as to be attracted to Magnet no matter which Magnet pole is brought toward the unmagnetised ironnickelcobalt. The ability of ferromagnetic material to retain its magnetisation after an external Field (physics) is removed is called its retentivity. Paramagnetic materials are materials like aluminium or platinum which become magnetised in an external Magnet Field (physics) in similar way to ferromagnetic materials. However they lose their Magnet when the external Magnet Field (physics) is removed. Diamagnetism is shown by materials like copper or bismuth which become mag- netised in Magnet Field (physics) with polarity opposite to the external Magnet Field (physics) Unlike iron they are slightly repelled by Magnet 
---------------------------------------------------------

8.4|The compass and the earth's magnetic field|173
Compass is an instrument which is used to find the Direction (geometry) of Magnet Field (physics) It can do this because Compass consists of small metal needle which is magnetised itself and which is free to turn in any Direction (geometry) Therefore when in the presence of Magnet Field (physics) the needle is able to line up in the same Direction (geometry) as the Field (physics) Lodestone magnetised form of iron-oxide was found to orientate itself in north-south Direction (geometry) if left free to rotate by suspension on string or on float in water. Lodestone was therefore used as an early navigational Compass Compass are mainly used in navigation to find Direction (geometry) on the earth. This Work (physics) because the earth itself has Magnet Field (physics) which is similar to that of bar Magnet (see the picture below). The Compass needle aligns with the Magnet Field (physics) Direction (geometry) and points north (or south). Once you know where north is you can figure out any other Direction (geometry) picture of Compass is shown below: Some animals can detect Magnet Field (physics) which helps them orientate themselves and find di- rection. Animals which can do this include pigeons bees Monarch butterflies sea turtles and fish. 
---------------------------------------------------------

8.4.1|The earth's magnetic field|175
In the picture below you can see representation of the earths Magnet Field (physics) which is very similar to the Magnet Field (physics) of giant bar Magnet like the one on the right of the picture. So the earth has two sets of north poles and south poles: geographic poles and Magnet poles. The earths Magnet Field (physics) is thought to be caused by churning liquid metals in the core which causes electric Electric current and Magnet Field (physics) From the picture you can see that the Direction (geometry) of Magnet north and true north are not identical. The geographic north pole which is the point through which the earths rotation axis goes is about 115o away from the Direction (geometry) of the Magnet north pole (which is where Compass will point). However the Magnet poles shift slightly all the time. Another interesting thing to note is that if we think of the earth as big bar Magnet and we know that Magnet Field (physics) lines always point from north to south then the Compass tells us that what we call the Magnet north pole is actually the south pole of the bar Magnet The Direction (geometry) of the earths Magnet Field (physics) flips Direction (geometry) about once every 200 000 years You can picture this as bar Magnet whose north and south pole periodically switch sides. The reason for this is still not fully understood. The earths Magnet Field (physics) is very important for humans and other animals on earth because it stops Electric charge particles emitted by the sun from hitting the earth and us. Electric charge particles can also damage and cause interference with telecommunications (such as cell phones). Electric charge particles (mainly protons and Electron are emitted by the sun in what is called the solar wind and travel towards the earth. These particles spiral in the earths Magnet Field (physics) towards the poles. If they Collision with other particles in the earths atmosphere they sometimes cause red or green Light or glow in the sky which is called the aurora. This happens close to the north and south pole and so we cannot see the aurora from South Africa.

9|Electrostatics|177

---------------------------------------------------------

9.1|Introduction|177
Electrostatics is the study of Electric charge which is static (not moving). 
---------------------------------------------------------

9.2|Two kinds of charge|177
All objects surrounding us (including people) contain large amounts of Electric charge There are two types of Electric charge Position (vector) Electric charge and Electric charge If the same amounts of negative and Position (vector) Electric charge are brought together they neutralise each other and there is no net Electric charge Neutral objects are objects which contain Position (vector) and Electric charge but in equal numbers. However if there is little bit more of one type of Electric charge than the other on the object then the object is said to be Electric charge The picture below shows what the distribution of Electric charge might look like for neutral Position (vector) Electric charge and Electric charge object. There are: Position (vector) Electric charge and Electric charge (-6) There is zero net Electric charge The object is neutral Position (vector) Electric charge and Electric charge (-6) The net Electric charge is +2 The object is Position (vector) Electric charge Position (vector) Electric charge and Electric charge (-9) -3 The net Electric charge is -3 The object is Electric charge 
---------------------------------------------------------

9.3|Unit of charge|177
Electric charge is measured in units called Coulomb (C). Coulomb of Electric charge is very large Electric charge In Electrostatics we therefore often Work (physics) with Electric charge in Coulomb (1 106 C) and Coulomb (1 nC 109 C). 
---------------------------------------------------------

9.4|Conservation of charge|177
Objects can become Electric charge by contact or by rubbing them. This means that they can gain extra negative or Position (vector) Electric charge Electric charge happens when you for example rub your feet against the carpet. When you then touch something metallic or another person you will feel shock as the excess Electric charge that you have collected is discharged. Important: Electric charge just like Energy cannot be created or destroyed. We say that Electric charge is conserved. When you rub your feet against the carpet Electric charge is transferred to you from the carpet. The carpet will then become Position (vector) Electric charge by the same amount. Another example is to take two neutral objects such as Plasticity (physics) ruler and cotton cloth (handkerchief). To begin the two objects are neutral (i.e. have the same amounts of Position (vector) and Electric charge +- +- +- +- -+- +- The ruler has postive Electric charge and The neutral cotton cloth has Position (vector) Electric charge and Electric charge The total number of Electric charge is: (9+5)14 Position (vector) Electric charge (9+5)14 Electric charge Electric charge BEFORE rubbing: Now if the cotton cloth is used to rub the ruler Electric charge is transferred from the cloth to the ruler. The ruler is now Electric charge and the cloth is Position (vector) Electric charge If you count up all the Position (vector) and Electric charge at the beginning and the end there are still the same amount. i.e. total Electric charge has been conserved +- +- +- +- -+- +- The ruler has postive Electric charge and The cotton cloth has Position (vector) Electric charge and Electric charge The total number of Electric charge is: (9+5)14 Position (vector) Electric charge (12+2)14 Electric charge 12 Electric charge AFTER rubbing: It is now Position (vector) Electric charge 
---------------------------------------------------------

9.5|Force between Charges|178
The Force exerted by non-moving (static) Electric charge on each other is called the Electrostatics Force The Electrostatics Force between: like Electric charge is repulsive opposite (unlike) Electric charge is attractive. In other words like Electric charge repel each other while opposite Electric charge attract each other. This is different to the gravitational Force which is only attractive. attractive Force repulsive Force repulsive Force The closer together the Electric charge are the stronger the Electrostatics Force between them. weaker repulsive Force stronger repulsive Force (shorter Distance between Electric charge (longer Distance between Electric charge Extension: Electrostatics Force The Electrostatics Force determines the arrangement of Electric charge on the surface of con- ductors. When we place Electric charge on spherical Electrical conductor the repulsive Force between the individual like Electric charge cause them to spread uniformly over the sur- face of the sphere. However for Electrical conductor with non-regular shapes there is concentration of Electric charge near the point or points of the object. This collection of Electric charge can actually allow Electric charge to leak off the Electrical conductor if the point is sharp enough. It is for this reason that buildings often have lightning rod on the roof to remove any Electric charge the building has collected. This minimises the possibility of the building being struck by lightning. This spreading out of Electric charge would not occur if we were to place the Electric charge on an Insulator (electricity) since Electric charge cannot move in Insulator (electricity) The word Electron comes from the Greek word for amber. The ancient Greeks observed that if you rubbed piece of amber you could use it to pick up bits of straw. 
---------------------------------------------------------

9.6|Conductors and insulators|181
All atoms are Electric charge i.e. they have the same amounts of negative and Position (vector) Electric charge inside them. By convention the Electron carry Electric charge and the protons carry Position (vector) Electric charge The basic unit of Electric charge called the elementary Electric charge is the amount of Electric charge carried by one Electron All the matter and materials on earth are made up of atoms. Some materials allow Electron to move relatively freely through them (e.g. most metals the human body). These materials are called Electrical conductor Other materials do not allow the Electric charge carriers the Electron to move through them (e.g. Plasticity (physics) glass). The Electron are bound to the atoms in the material. These materials are called non-conductors or Insulator (electricity) If an excess of Electric charge is placed on an Insulator (electricity) it will stay where it is put and there will be concentration of Electric charge in that area of the object. However if an excess of Electric charge is placed on Electrical conductor the like Electric charge will repel each other and spread out over the surface of the object. When two Electrical conductor are made to touch the total Electric charge on them is shared between the two. If the two Electrical conductor are identical then each Electrical conductor will be left with half of the total Electric charge Extension: Electric charge and Electron The basic unit of Electric charge namely the elementary Electric charge is carried by the Electron (equal to 1.6021019 C). In conducting material (e.g. copper) when the atoms bond to form the material some of the outermost loosely bound Electron become detached from the individual atoms and so become free to move around. The Electric charge carried by these Electron can move around in the material. In Insulator (electricity) there are very few if any free Electron and so the Electric charge cannot move around in the material. 
---------------------------------------------------------

9.6.1|The electroscope|182
The Electroscope is very sensitive instrument which can be used to detect Electric charge diagram of gold leaf Electroscope is shown the figure below. The Electroscope consists of glass container with metal rod inside which has thin pieces of gold foil attached. The other end of the metal rod has metal plate attached to it outside the glass container. The Electroscope detects Electric charge in the following way: Electric charge object like the Position (vector) Electric charge rod in the picture is brought close to (but not touching) the neutral metal plate of the Electroscope This causes Electric charge in the gold foil metal rod and metal plate to be attracted to the Position (vector) rod. Because the metal (gold is metal too) is Electrical conductor the Electric charge can move freely from the foil up the metal rod and onto the metal plate. There is now more Electric charge on the plate and more Position (vector) Electric charge on the gold foil leaves. This is called inducing Electric charge on the metal plate. It is important to remember that the Electroscope is still neutral (the total Position (vector) and Electric charge are the same) the Electric charge have just been induced to move to different parts of the instrument The induced Position (vector) Electric charge on the gold leaves Force them apart since like Electric charge repel This is how we can tell that the rod is Electric charge If the rod is now moved away from the metal plate the Electric charge in the Electroscope will spread itself out evenly again and the leaves will fall down again because there will no longer be an induced Electric charge on them. Grounding If you were to bring the Electric charge rod close to the uncharged Electroscope and then you touched the metal plate with your finger at the same time this would cause Electric charge to flow up from the ground (the earth) through your body onto the metal plate. This is called grounding. The Electric charge flowing onto the plate is opposite to the Electric charge on the rod since it is attracted to the rod. Therefore for our picture the Electric charge flowing onto the plate would be negative. Now Electric charge has been added to the Electroscope It is no longer neutral but has an excess of Electric charge Now if we move the rod away the leaves will remain apart because they have an excess of Electric charge and they repel each other. 
---------------------------------------------------------

9.7|Attraction between charged and uncharged objects|183

---------------------------------------------------------

9.7.1|Polarisation of Insulators|183
Unlike Electrical conductor the Electron in Insulator (electricity) (non-conductors) are bound to the atoms of the Insulator (electricity) and cannot move around freely in the material. However Electric charge object can still exert Force on neutral Insulator (electricity) through the concept of polarisation. If Position (vector) Electric charge rod is brought close to neutral Insulator (electricity) such as polystyrene it can attract the bound Electron to move round to the side of the atoms which is closest to the rod and cause the Position (vector) nuclei to move slightly to the opposite side of the atoms. This process is called polarisation. Although it is very small Optical microscope effect if there are many atoms and the polarised object is Light (e.g. small polystyrene ball) it can add up to enough Force to be attracted onto the Electric charge rod. Remember that the polystyrene is only polarised not Electric charge The polystyrene ball is still neutral since no Electric charge was added or removed from it. The picture shows not-to-scale view of the polarised atoms in the polystyrene ball: Some materials are made up of molecules which are already polarised. These are molecules which have more Position (vector) and more negative side but are still neutral overall. Just as polarised polystyrene ball can be attracted to Electric charge rod these materials are also affected if brought close to Electric charge object. Water is an example of substance which is made of polarised molecules. If Position (vector) Electric charge rod is brought close to stream of water the molecules can rotate so that the negative sides all line up towards the rod. The stream of water will then be attracted to the rod since opposite Electric charge attract. 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.1|Electric Circuits|187
In South Africa people depend on electricity to provide Power (physics) for most appliances in the home at Work (physics) and out in the world in general. For example flourescent Light electric heating and cooking (on electric stoves) all depend on electricity to Work (physics) To realise just how big an impact electricity has on our daily lives just think about what happens when there is Power (physics) failure or load shedding. Make sure you have someone with you who knows if what you are doing is safe. Normal electrical outlets are dangerous. Treat electricity with respect in your everyday life.

10.2|Potential Difference|192

---------------------------------------------------------

10.2.1|Potential Difference|192
When circuit is connected and is complete circuit Electric charge can move through the circuit. Electric charge will not move unless there is reason Force Think of it as though Electric charge is at rest and something has to push it along. This means that Work (physics) needs to be done to make Electric charge move. Force acts on the Electric charge doing Work (physics) to make them move. The Force is provided by the battery in the circuit. We call the moving Electric charge Electric current and we will talk about this later. The Position (vector) of the Electric charge in the circuit tells you how much Potential energy it has because of the Force being exerted on it. This is like the Force from Gravity the higher an object is above the ground Position (vector) the more Potential energy it has. The amount of Work (physics) to move Electric charge from one point to another point is how much the Potential energy has changed. This is the difference in Potential energy called Voltage Notice that it is difference between the value of Potential energy at two points so we say that Voltage is measured between or across two points. We do not say Voltage through something. Definition: Voltage Electric potential as the difference in Electric potential energy per unit Electric charge between two points. The units of Voltage are the volt (V). The units are volt (V) which is the same as Joule per Coulomb the amount of Work (physics) done per unit Electric charge Electric potential is also called Voltage 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.2.2|Potential Difference and Parallel Resistors|193
When resistors are connected in parallel the start and end points for all the resistors are the same. These points have the same Potential energy and so the Voltage between them is the same no matter what is put in between them. You can have one two or many resistors between the two points the Voltage will not change. You can ignore whatever components are between two points in circuit when calculating the difference between the two points. Look at the following circuit diagrams. The battery is the same in all cases all that changes is more resistors are added between the points marked by the black dots. If we were to measure the Voltage between the two dots in these circuits we would get the same answer for all three cases. Lets look at two resistors in parallel more closely. When you construct circuit you use wires and you might think that measuring the Voltage in different places on the wires will make difference. This is not true. The Voltage or Voltage measurement will only be different if you measure different set of components. All points on the wires that have no circuit components between them will give you the same measurements. All three of the measurements shown in the picture below will give you the same Voltage The different measurement points on the left have no components between them so there is no change in Potential energy Exactly the same applies to the different points on the right. When you measure the Voltage between the points on the left and right you will get the same answer. 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.2.3|Potential Difference and Series Resistors|194
When resistors are in series one after the other there is Voltage across each resistor. The total Voltage across set of resistors in series is the sum of the Voltage across each of the resistors in the set. This is the same as falling large Distance under Gravity or falling that same Distance (difference) in many smaller steps. The total Distance (difference) is the same. Look at the circuits below. If we measured the Voltage between the black dots in all of these circuits it would be the same just like we saw above. So we now know the total Voltage is the same across one two or three resistors. We also know that some Work (physics) is required to make Electric charge flow through each one each is step down in Potential energy These steps add up to the total drop which we know is the difference between the two dots. Let us look at this in bit more detail. In the picture below you can see what the different measurements for identical resistors in series could look like. The total Voltage across all three resistors is the sum of the Voltage across the individual resistors. 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.2.4|Ohm's Law|194
The Voltage is the change in Potential energy or Work (physics) done when Electric charge moves between two points in the circuit. The greater the Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance to Electric charge moving the more Work (physics) that needs to be done. The Work (physics) done or Voltage thus depends on the Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance The Voltage is proportional to the Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance Definition: Ohm Law Voltage across circuit component is proportional to the Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of the component. Use the fact that Voltage is proportional to Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance to calculate what proportion of the total Voltage of circuit will be found across each circuit element. We know that the total Voltage is equal to V1 in the first circuit to V1 V2 in the second circuit and V1 V2 V3 in the third circuit. We know that the Potential energy lost across resistor is proportional to the Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of the component. The total Voltage is shared evenly across the total Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of the circuit. This means that the Voltage per unit of Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance is Then the Voltage across resistor is just the Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance times the Voltage per unit of Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.2.5|EMF|195
When you measure the Voltage across (or between) the terminals of battery you are measuring the electromotive Force Electromotive force of the battery. This is how much Potential energy the battery has to make Electric charge move through the circuit. This driving Potential energy is equal to the total Potential energy drops in the circuit. This means that the Voltage across the battery is equal to the sum of the Voltage in the circuit. We can use this information to solve problems in which the Voltage across elements in circuit add up to the Electromotive force Electromotive force Vtotal

10.3|Current|198

---------------------------------------------------------

10.3.1|Flow of Charge|198
We have been talking about moving Electric charge We need to be able to deal with numbers how much Electric charge is moving how fast is it moving? The concept that gives us this information is called Electric current Electric current allows us to quantify the movement of Electric charge When we talk about Electric current we talk about how much Electric charge moves past fixed point in circuit in one second. Think of Electric charge being pushed around the circuit by the battery there are Electric charge in the wires but unless there is battery they wont move. When one Electric charge moves the Electric charge next to it also move. They keep their spacing. If you had tube of marbles like in this picture. marble marble If you push one marble into the tube one must come out the other side. If you look at any point in the tube and push one marble into the tube one marble will move past the point you are looking at. This is similar to Electric charge in the wires of circuit. If Electric charge moves they all move and the same number move at every point in the circuit. 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.3.2|Current|198
Now that weve thought about the moving Electric charge and visualised what is happening we need to get back to quantifying moving Electric charge Ive already told you that we use Electric current but we still need to define it. Definition: Electric current Electric current is the rate at which Electric charge moves past fixed point in circuit. We use the symbol to show Electric current and it is measured in amperes (A). One ampere is one Coulomb of Electric charge moving in one second. When Electric current flows in circuit we show this on diagram by adding arrows. The arrows show the Direction (geometry) of flow in circuit. By convention we say that Electric charge flows from the Position (vector) terminal on battery to the negative terminal. 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.3.3|Series Circuits|199
In Series and parallel circuits the Electric charge has single path from the battery returning to the battery. The arrows in this picture show you the Direction (geometry) that Electric charge will flow in the circuit. They dont show you much Electric charge will flow only the Direction (geometry) Benjamin Franklin made guess about the Direction (geometry) of Electric charge flow when rubbing smooth wax with rough wool. He thought that the Electric charge flowed from the wax to the wool (i.e. from Position (vector) to negative) which was opposite to the real Direction (geometry) Due to this Electron are said to have Electric charge and so objects which Ben Franklin called negative (meaning shortage of Electric charge really have an excess of Electron By the time the true Direction (geometry) of Electron flow was discovered the convention of Position (vector) and negative had already been so well accepted in the scientific world that no effort was made to change it. Important: cell does not produce the same amount of Electric current no matter what is connected to it. While the Voltage produced by cell is constant the amount of Electric current supplied depends on what is in the circuit. How does the Electric current through the battery in circuit with several resistors in series compare to the Electric current in circuit with single resistor?

10.3.4|Parallel Circuits|200
How does the Electric current through the battery in circuit with several resistors in parallel compare to the Electric current in circuit with single resistor? Why is this the case? Why do more resistors make it easier for Electric charge to flow in the circuit? It is because they are in parallel so there are more paths for Electric charge to take to move. You can think of it like highway with more lanes or the tube of marbles splitting into multiple parallel tubes. The more branches there are the easier it is for Electric charge to flow. You will learn more about the total Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of parallel resistors later but always remember that more resistors in parallel mean more pathways. In series the pathways come one after the other so it does not make it easier for Electric charge to flow. 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.4|Resistance|202

---------------------------------------------------------

10.4.1|What causes resistance?|202
We have spoken about resistors that slow down the flow of Electric charge in Electrical conductor On Optical microscope level Electron moving through the Electrical conductor Collision with the particles of which the Electrical conductor (metal) is made. When they Collision they transfer kinetic Energy The Electron therefore lose kinetic Energy and slow down. This leads to Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance The transferred Energy causes the Electrical conductor to heat up. You can feel this directly if you touch cellphone charger when you are Electric charge cell phone the charger gets warm Definition: Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance slows down the flow of Electric charge in circuit. We use the symbol to show Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance and it is measured in units called Ohm with the symbol Ohm Volt Ampere All Electrical conductor have some Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance For example piece of wire has less Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance than Light bulb but both have Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance The high Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of the filament (small wire) in lightbulb causes the Electron to transfer lot of their kinetic Energy in the form of heat. The heat Energy is enough to cause the filament to glow white-hot which produces Light The wires connecting the lamp to the cell or battery hardly even get warm while conducting the same amount of Electric current This is because of their much lower Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance due to their larger cross-section (they are thicker). An important effect of resistor is that it converts electrical Energy into other forms of Energy such as heat and Light There is special type of Electrical conductor called superconductor that has no Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance but the materials that make up superconductors only start supercon- ducting at very low Temperature (approximately -170C). Why do batteries go flat? battery stores chemical Potential energy When it is connected in circuit chemical reaction takes place inside the battery which converts chemical Potential energy to electrical Energy which Power (physics) the Electron to move through the circuit. All the circuit elements (such as the conducting leads resistors and lightbulbs) have some Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance to the flow of Electric charge and convert the electrical Energy to heat andor Light The battery goes flat when all its chemical Potential energy has been converted into other forms of Energy 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.4.2|Resistors in electric circuits|202
It is important to understand what effect adding resistors to circuit has on the total Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of circuit and on the Electric current that can flow in the circuit. Resistors in series When we add resistors in series to circuit we increase the Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance to the flow of Electric current There is only one path that the Electric current can flow down and the Electric current is the same at all places in the Series and parallel circuits Take look at the diagram below: On the left there is circuit with single resistor and battery. No matter where we measure the Electric current it is the same in Series and parallel circuits On the right we have added second resistor in series to the circuit. The total Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of the circuit has increased and you can see from the reading on the Ammeter that the Electric current in the circuit has decreased. Resistors in parallel In contrast to the series case when we add resistors in parallel we create more paths along which Electric current can flow. By doing this we decrease the total Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of the circuit Take look at the diagram below. On the left we have the same circuit as in the previous diagram with battery and resistor. The Ammeter shows Electric current of ampere. On the right we have added second resistor in parallel to the first resistor. This has increased the number of paths (branches) the Electric charge can take through the circuit the total Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance has decreased. You can see that the Electric current in the circuit has increased. Also notice that the Electric current in the different branches can be different. 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.5|Instruments to Measure voltage, current and resistance|204
As we have seen in previous sections an electric circuit is made up of number of different components such as batteries resistors and Light bulbs. There are devices to measure the properties of these components. These devices are called Metre For example one may be interested in measuring the amount of Electric current flowing through circuit using an Ammeter or measuring the Voltage provided by battery using Voltmeter In this section we will discuss the practical usage of Voltmeter Ammeter and Ohmmeter 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.5.1|Voltmeter|204
Voltmeter is an instrument for measuring the Voltage between two points in an electric circuit. In analogy with water circuit Voltmeter is like Metre designed to measure pressure difference. Since one is interested in measuring the Voltage between two points in circuit Voltmeter must be connected in parallel with the portion of the circuit on which the measurement is made. Figure 10.3: Voltmeter should be connected in parallel in circuit. Figure 10.3 shows Voltmeter connected in parallel with battery. One lead of the Voltmeter is connected to one end of the battery and the other lead is connected to the opposite end. The Voltmeter may also be used to measure the Voltage across resistor or any other component of circuit that has Voltage drop. 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.5.2|Ammeter|204
An Ammeter is an instrument used to measure the flow of electric Electric current in circuit. Since one is interested in measuring the Electric current flowing through circuit component the Ammeter must be connected in series with the measured circuit component (Figure 10.4). 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.5.3|Ohmmeter|204
An Ohmmeter is an instrument for measuring electrical Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance The basic Ohmmeter can function much like an Ammeter The Ohmmeter Work (physics) by suppling constant Voltage to the resistor and measuring the Electric current flowing through it. The measured Electric current is then converted into corresponding Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance reading through Ohm Law. Ohmmeter only function correctly when measuring Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance that is not being Power (physics) by Voltage or Electric current source. In other words you cannot measure the Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of component that is already connected to circuit. This is because the Ohmmeter accurate indication depends only on its own source of Voltage The presence of any other Voltage across the measured circuit component interferes with the Ohmmeter operation. Figure 10.5 shows an Ohmmeter connected with resistor. 
---------------------------------------------------------

10.5.4|Meters Impact on Circuit|205
good quality Metre used correctly will not significantly change the values it is used to measure. This means that an Ammeter has very low Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance to not slow down the flow of Electric charge Voltmeter has very high Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance so that it does not add another parallel pathway to the circuit for the Electric charge to flow along.
