24|Doppler Effect|533

---------------------------------------------------------

24.1|Introduction|533
Have you noticed how the Pitch (music) of car hooter changes as the car passes by or how the Pitch (music) of radio box on the pavement changes as you drive by? This effect is known as the Doppler effect and will be studied in this chapter. The Doppler effect is named after Johann Christian Andreas Doppler (29 November 1803 17 March 1853) an Austrian mathematician and physicist who first explained the phenomenon in 1842. 
---------------------------------------------------------

24.2|The Doppler Effect with Sound and Ultrasound|533
As seen in the introduction there are two situations which lead to the Doppler effect 1. When the source moves relative to the observer for example the Pitch (music) of car hooter as it passes by. 2. When the observer moves relative to the source for example the Pitch (music) of radio on the pavement as you drive by. Definition: Doppler effect The Doppler effect is the apparent change in Frequency and Wavelength of Wave when the observer and the source of the Wave move relative to each other. We experience the Doppler effect quite often in our lives without realising that it is science taking place. The changing Sound of taxi hooter or ambulance as it drives past are examples of this as you have seen in the introduction. The question is how does the Doppler effect take place. Let us consider source of Sound Wave with constant Frequency and Amplitude The Sound Wave can be drawn as concentric circles where each circle represents another wavefront like in figure 24.1 below. The Sound source is the dot in the middle and is stationary. For the Doppler effect to take place the source must be moving. Lets consider the following situation: The source (dot) emits one peak (represented by circle) that moves away from the source at the same rate in all Direction (geometry) As this peak moves away the source also moves and then emits the second peak. Now the two circles are not concentric any more but on the one side they are closer together and on the other side they are further apart. This is shown in the next diagram. If the source continues moving at the same Speed in the same Direction (geometry) (i.e. with the same Velocity which you will learn more about later). then the Distance between peaks on the right of the source is the constant. The Distance between peaks on the left is also constant but they are different on the left and right. This means that the time between peaks on the right is less so the Frequency is higher. It is higher than on the left and higher than if the source were not moving at all. On the left hand side the peaks are further apart than on the right and further apart than if the source were at rest this means the Frequency is lower. When car appoaches you the Sound Wave that reach you have shorter Wavelength and higher Frequency You hear higher Sound When the car moves away from you the Sound Wave that reach you have longer Wavelength and lower Frequency You hear lower Sound This change in Frequency can be calculated by using: where fL is the Frequency perceived by the listener fS is the Frequency of the source is the Speed of the Wave vL the Speed of the listener and vS the Speed of the source. Radar-based speed-traps use the Doppler effect The radar gun emits radio Wave of specific Frequency When the car is standing still the Wave Reflection (physics) Wave are the same Frequency as the Wave emitted by the radar gun. When the car is moving the Doppler Frequency shift can be used to determine the Speed of the car. 
---------------------------------------------------------

24.2.1|Ultrasound and the Doppler Effect|537
Ultrasonic Wave (ultrasound) are Sound Wave with Frequency greater than 20 000 Hertz (the upper limit of hearing). These Wave can be used in medicine to determine the Direction (geometry) of blood flow. The device called Doppler flow Metre sends out Sound Wave The Sound Wave can travle through skin and tissue and will be Reflection (physics) by moving objects in the body (like blood). The Reflection (physics) Wave return to the flow Metre where its Frequency (received Frequency is compared to the transmitted Frequency Because of the Doppler effect blood that is moving towards the flow Metre will change the Sound to higher Frequency (blue shift) and blood that is moving away from the flow Metre will cause lower Frequency (red shift). Ultrasound can be used to determine whether blood is flowing in the right Direction (geometry) in the circulation system of unborn babies or identify areas in the body where blood flow is restricted due to narrow veins. The use of ultrasound equipment in medicine is called sonography or ultrasonography. 
---------------------------------------------------------

24.3|The Doppler Effect with Light|537
Light is Wave and earlier you learnt how you can study the properties of one Wave and apply the same ideas to another Wave The same applies to Sound and Light We know the Doppler effect affects Sound Wave when the source is moving. Therefore if we apply the Doppler effect to Light the Frequency of the emitted Light should change when the source of the Light is moving relative to the observer. When the Frequency of Sound Wave changes the Sound you hear changes. When the Frequency of Light changes the Color you would see changes. This means that the Doppler effect can be observed by change in Sound (for Sound Wave and change in Color (for Light Wave Keep in mind that there are Sound that we cannot hear (for example ultrasound) and Light that we cannot see (for example ultraviolet Light We can apply all the ideas that we learnt about the Doppler effect to Light When talking about Light we use slightly different names to describe what happens. If you look at the Color spectrum (more details Chapter 30) then you will see that blue Light has shorter Wavelength than red Light If you are in the middle of the visible Color then longer Wavelength are more red and shorter Wavelength are more blue. So we call shifts towards longer Wavelength red-shifts and shifts towards shorter Wavelength blue-shifts. shift in Wavelength is the same as shift in Frequency Longer Wavelength of Light have lower Frequency and shorter Wavelength have higher Frequency From the Doppler effect we know that when things move towards you any Wave they emit that you measure are shifted to shorter Wavelength (blueshifted). If things move away from you the shift is to longer Wavelength (redshifted). 
---------------------------------------------------------

24.3.1|The Expanding Universe|538
Stars emit Light which is why we can see them at night. Galaxies are huge collections of stars. An example is our own Galaxy the Milky Way of which our sun is only one of the millions of stars Using large Telescope like the Southern African Large Telescope (SALT) in the Karoo astronomers can measure the Light from distant galaxies. The spectrum of Light (see Chapter ??) can tell us what elements are in the stars in the galaxies because each element emitsabsorbs Light at particular Wavelength (called spectral lines). If these lines are observed to be shifted from their usual Wavelength to shorter Wavelength then the Light from the galaxy is said to be blueshifted. If the spectral lines are shifted to longer Wavelength then the Light from the galaxy is said to be redshifted. If we think of the blueshift and redshift in Doppler effect terms then blueshifted galaxy would appear to be moving towards us (the observers) and redshifted galaxy would appear to be moving away from us. Important: If the Light source is moving away from the observer Position (vector) Velocity then the observed Frequency is lower and the observed Wavelength is greater (redshifted). If the source is moving towards (negative Velocity the observer the observed fre- quency is higher and the Wavelength is shorter (blueshifted). Edwin Hubble (20 November 1889 28 September 1953) measured the Doppler shift of large sample of galaxies. He found that the Light from distant galaxies is redshifted and he discovered that there is proportionality relationship between the redshift and the Distance to the galaxy. Galaxies that are further away always appear more redshifted than nearby galaxies. Remember that redshift in Doppler terms means Velocity of the Light source away from the observer. So why do all distant galaxies appear to be moving away from our Galaxy? The reason is that the universe is expanding The galaxies are not actually moving themselves rather the space between them is expanding 
---------------------------------------------------------

25.1|Introduction|541
We call the Light that we humans can see visible Light Visible Light is actually just small part of the large spectrum of Electromagnetic radiation which you will learn more about in Chapter 30. We can think of Electromagnetic radiation and visible Light as transverse Wave We know that transverse Wave can be described by their Amplitude Frequency (or Wavelength and Velocity The Velocity of Wave is given by the product of its Frequency and Wavelength (25.1) However Electromagnetic radiation including visible Light is special because no matter what the Frequency it all moves at constant Velocity (in vacuum) which is known as the Speed of Light The Speed of Light has the symbol and is: 108 m.s1 Since the Speed of Light is we can then say:

25.2|Colour and Light|541
Our eyes are sensitive to visible Light over range of Wavelength from 390 nm to 780 nm (1 nm 109 m). The different Color of Light we see are related to specific Frequency (and Wavelength of visible Light The Wavelength and Frequency are listed in table 25.1. You can see from table 25.1 that violet Light has the shortest Wavelength and highest Frequency while red Light has the longest Wavelength and lowest Frequency

25.2.1|Dispersion of white light|544
White Light like the Light which comes from the sun is made up of all the visible Wavelength of Light In other words white Light is combination of all the Color of visible Light In Chapter you learnt that the Speed of Light is different in different substances. The Speed of Light in different substances depends on the Frequency of the Light For example when white Light travels through glass Light of the different Frequency is slowed down by different amounts. The lower the Frequency the less the Speed is reduced which means that red Light (lowest Frequency is slowed down less than violet Light (highest Frequency We can see this when white Light is incident on glass prism. Have look at the picture below. When the white Light hits the edge of the prism the Light which travels through the glass is Refraction as it moves from the less dense medium (air) to the more dense medium (glass). The red Light which is slowed down the least is Refraction the least. The violet Light which is slowed down the most is Refraction the most. When the Light hits the other side of the prism it is again Refraction but the angle of the prism edge allows the Light to remain separated into its different Color White Light is therefore separated into its different Color by the prism and we say that the white Light has been dispersed by the prism. The dispersion effect is also responsible for why we see rainbows. When sunlight hits drops of water in the atmosphere the white Light is dispersed into its different Color by the water. 
---------------------------------------------------------

25.3|Addition and Subtraction of Light|544

---------------------------------------------------------

25.3.1|Additive Primary Colours|544
The primary Color of Light are red green and blue. When all the primary Color are superposed (added together) white Light is produced. Red green and blue are therefore called the additive primary Color All the other Color can be produced by different combinations of red green and blue. 
---------------------------------------------------------

25.3.2|Subtractive Primary Colours|545
The subtractive primary Color are obtained by subtracting one of the three additive primary Color from white Light The subtractive primary Color are yellow magenta and cyan. Magenta appears as pinkish-purplish Color and cyan looks greenish-blue. You can see how the primary Color of Light add up to the different subtractive Color in the illustration below. 
---------------------------------------------------------

25.3.3|Complementary Colours|546
Complementary Color are two Color of Light which add together to give white. You should have found that the complementary Color for red green and blue are: Red and Cyan Green and Magenta Blue and Yellow 
---------------------------------------------------------

25.3.4|Perception of Colour|546
The light-sensitive lining on the back inside half of the human eye is called the retina. The retina contains two kinds of Light sensitive cells or photoreceptors: the rod cells (sensitive to low Light and the cone cells (sensitive to normal daylight) which enable us to see. The rods are not very sensitive to Color but Work (physics) well in dimly lit conditions. This is why it is possible to see in dark room but it is Hardness to see any Color Only your rods are sensitive to the low Light levels and so you can only see in black white and grey. The cones enable us to see Color Normally there are three kinds of cones each containing different Pigment The cones are activated when the Pigment absorb Light The three types of cones are sensitive to (i.e. absorb) red blue and green Light respectively. Therefore we can perceive all the different Color in the visible spectrum when the different types of cones are stimulated by different amounts since they are just combinations of the three primary Color of Light The rods and cones have different response times to Light The cones react quickly when bright Light falls on them. The rods take longer time to react. This is why it takes while (about 10 minutes) for your eyes to adjust when you enter dark room after being outside on sunny day. Color blindness in humans is the inability to perceive differences between some or all Color that other people can see. Most often it is genetic problem but may also occur because of eye nerve or brain damage or due to exposure to certain chemicals. The most common forms of human Color blindness result from problems with either the middle or long Wavelength sensitive cone systems and involve difficulties in discriminating reds yellows and greens from one another. This is called red-green Color blindness. Other forms of Color blindness are much rarer. They include problems in discriminating blues from yellows and the rarest forms of all complete Color blindness or monochromasy where one cannot distinguish any Color from grey as in black-and-white movie or photograph. 
---------------------------------------------------------

25.3.5|Colours on a Television Screen|547
If you look very closely at Color cathode-ray television screen or computer screen you will see that there are very many small red green and blue dots called phosphors on it. These dots are caused to fluoresce (glow brightly) when beam of Electron from the cathode-ray tube behind the screen hits them. Since different combinations of the three primary Color of Light can produce any other Color only red green and blue dots are needed to make pictures containing all the Color of the visible spectrum. 
---------------------------------------------------------

25.4|Pigments and Paints|548
We have learnt that white Light is combination of all the Color of the visible spectrum and that each Color of Light is related to different Frequency But what gives everyday objects around us their different Color Pigment are substances which give an object its Color by absorbing certain Frequency of Light and Reflection (physics) other Frequency For example red Pigment absorbs all Color of Light except red which it Reflection (physics) Paints and inks contain Pigment which gives the paints and inks different Color 
---------------------------------------------------------

25.4.1|Colour of opaque objects|548
Objects which you cannot see through (i.e. they are not transparent) are called opaque. Examples of some opaque objects are metals wood and bricks. The Color of an opaque object is determined by the Color (therefore Frequency of Light which it Reflection (physics) For example when white Light strikes blue opaque object such as ruler the ruler will absorb all Frequency of Light except blue which will be Reflection (physics) The Reflection (physics) blue Light is the Light which makes it into our eyes and therefore the object will appear blue. Opaque objects which appear white do not absorb any Light They Reflection (physics) all the Frequency Black opaque objects absorb all Frequency of Light They do not Reflection (physics) at all and therefore appear to have no Color 
---------------------------------------------------------

25.4.2|Colour of transparent objects|548
If an object is transparent it means that you can see through it. For example glass clean water and some clear Plasticity (physics) are transparent. The Color of transparent object is determined by the Color Frequency of Light which it transmits (allows to pass through it). For example cup made of green glass will appear green because it absorbs all the other Frequency of Light except green which it transmits. This is the Light which we receive in our eyes and the object appears green. 
---------------------------------------------------------

25.4.3|Pigment primary colours|549
The primary Pigment and paints are cyan magenta and yellow. When Pigment or paints of these three Color are mixed together in equal amounts they produce black. Any other Color of paint can be made by mixing the primary Pigment together in different quantities. The primary Pigment are related to the primary Color of Light in the following way: Color printers only use Color of ink: cyan magenta yellow and black. All the other Color can be mixed from these

26|2D and 3D Wavefronts|553

26.2|Wavefronts|553
Consider three point sources of Wave If each source emits Wave isotropically (i.e. the same in all Direction (geometry) we will get the situation shown in as shown in Figure 26.1. We define wavefront as the imaginary line that joins Wave that are in phase. These are indicated by the grey vertical lines in Figure 26.1. The points that are in phase can be peaks Crest (physics) or anything in between it doesnt matter which points you choose as long as they are in phase. Figure 26.1: Wavefronts are imaginary lines joining Wave that are in phase. In the example the wavefronts (shown by the grey vertical lines) join all Wave at the Crest (physics) of their cycle.

26.3|The Huygens Principle|554
Christiaan Huygens described how to determine the path of Wave through medium. Definition: The HuygensFresnel principle Each point on wavefront acts like point source of circular Wave The Wave emitted from these point sources interfere to form another wavefront. simple example of the HuygensFresnel principle is to consider the single wavefront in Figure 26.2. Christiaan Huygens (14 April 1629 July 1695) was Dutch mathematician astronomer and physicist born in The Hague as the son of Constantijn Huygens. He studied law at the University of Leiden and the College of Orange in Breda before turning to science. Historians commonly associate Huygens with the scientific revolution. Huygens generally receives minor credit for his role in the development of modern calculus. He also achieved note for his arguments that Light consisted of Wave see: wave-particle duality. In 1655 he discovered Saturns moon Titan. He also examined Saturns planetary rings and in 1656 he discovered that those rings consisted of rocks. In the same year he observed and sketched the Orion Nebula. He also discovered several interstellar nebulae and some double stars. 
---------------------------------------------------------

26.4|Interference|556
Interference occurs when two identical Wave pass through the same region of space at the same time resulting in superposition of Wave There are two types of interference which is of interest: constructive interference and destructive interference. Constructive interference occurs when both Wave have Displacement (vector) in the same Direction (geometry) while destructive interference occurs when one Wave has Displacement (vector) in the opposite Direction (geometry) to the other thereby resulting in cancellation. There is no Displacement (vector) of the medium in destructive interference while for constructive interference the Displacement (vector) of the medium is greater than the individual Displacement (vector) Constructive interference occurs when both Wave have Displacement (vector) in the same Direction (geometry) this means they both have peak or they both have Crest (physics) at the same place at the same time. If they both have peak then the peaks add together to form bigger peak. If they both have Crest (physics) then the Crest (physics) gets deeper. Destructive interference occurs when one Wave has Displacement (vector) in the opposite Direction (geometry) to the other this means that the one Wave has peak and the other Wave has Crest (physics) If the Wave have identical magnitudes then the peak fills up the Crest (physics) and the medium will look like there are no Wave at that point. There will be no Displacement (vector) of the medium. place where destructive interference takes places is called node. Wave can interfere at places where there is never Crest (physics) and Crest (physics) or peak and peak or Crest (physics) and peak at the same time. At these places the Wave will add together and the resultant Displacement (vector) will be the sum of the two Wave but they wont be points of maximum interference. Consider the two identical Wave shown in the picture below. The wavefronts of the peaks are shown as black lines while the wavefronts of the Crest (physics) are shown as grey lines. You can see that the black lines cross other black lines in many places. This means two peaks are in the same place at the same time so we will have constructive interference where the two peaks add together to form bigger peak. Two points sources (A and B) radiate identical Wave The wavefronts of the peaks (black lines) and Crest (physics) (grey lines) are shown. Constructive interference occurs where two black lines intersect or where two gray lines intersect. Destructive interference occurs where black line intersects with grey line. You can see that the black lines cross other black lines in many places. This means two peaks are in the same place at the same time so we will have constructive interference where the two peaks add together to form bigger peak. When the grey lines cross other grey lines there are two Crest (physics) are in the same place at the same time so we will have constructive interference where the two Crest (physics) add together to form bigger Crest (physics) In the case where grey line crosses black line we are seeing Crest (physics) and peak in the same place. These will cancel each other out and the medium will have no Displacement (vector) at that point. black line black line peak peak constructive interference grey line grey line Crest (physics) Crest (physics) constructive interference black line grey line grey line black line peak Crest (physics) Crest (physics) peak destructive interference On half the picture below we have marked the constructive interference with solid black diamond and the destructive interference with hollow diamond. To see if you understand it cover up the half we have marked with diamonds and try to Work (physics) out which points are constructive and destructive on the other half of the picture. The two halves are Mirror image of each other so you can check yourself.

26.5|Diffraction|557
One of the most interesting and also very useful properties of Wave is Diffraction Definition: Diffraction Diffraction is the ability of Wave to spread out in wavefronts as the Wave passes through small aperture or around sharp edge. Extension: Diffraction Diffraction refers to various phenomena associated with Wave propagation such as the bending spreading and interference of Wave emerging from an aperture. It occurs with any type of Wave including Sound Wave water Wave electromagnetic Wave such as Light and radio Wave While Diffraction always occurs its effects are generally only noticeable for Wave where the Wavelength is on the order of the feature size of the Diffraction objects or apertures. For example if two rooms are connected by an open doorway and Sound is produced in remote corner of one of them person in the other room will hear the Sound as if it originated at the doorway. As far as the second room is concerned the vibrating air in the doorway is the source of the Sound The same is true of Light passing the edge of an obstacle but this is not as easily observed because of the short Wavelength of visible Light This means that when Wave move through small holes they appear to bend around the sides because there are not enough points on the wavefront to form another straight wavefront. This is bending round the sides we call Diffraction Extension: Diffraction Diffraction effects are more clear for water Wave with longer Wavelength Diffraction can be demonstrated by placing small barriers and obstacles in ripple tank and observing the path of the water Wave as they encounter the obstacles. The Wave are seen to pass around the barrier into the regions behind it subsequently the water behind the barrier is disturbed. The amount of Diffraction (the sharpness of the bending) increases with increasing Wavelength and decreases with decreasing Wavelength In fact when the Wavelength of the Wave are smaller than the obstacle no noticeable Diffraction occurs. 
---------------------------------------------------------

26.5.1|Diffraction through a Slit|558
When Wave strikes barrier with hole only part of the Wave can move through the hole. If the hole is similar in size to the Wavelength of the Wave Diffraction occurs. The Wave that comes through the hole no longer looks like straight Wave front. It bends around the edges of the hole. If the hole is small enough it acts like point source of circular Wave Now if allow the wavefront to impinge on barrier with hole in it then only the points on the wavefront that move into the hole can continue emitting forward moving Wave but because lot of the wavefront have been removed the points on the edges of the hole emit Wave that bend round the edges. If you employ HuygensFresnel principle you can see the effect is that the wavefronts are no longer straight lines. Each point of the slit acts like point source. If we think about the two point sources on the edges of the slit and call them and then we can go back to the diagram we had earlier but with some parts block by the wall. If this diagram were showing Sound Wave then the Sound would be louder (constructive interference) in some places and quieter (destructive interference) in others. You can start to see that there will be pattern (interference pattern) to the louder and quieter places. If we were studying Light Wave then the Light would be brighter in some places than others depending on the interferences. The intensity (how bright or loud) of the interference pattern for single narrow slit looks like this: The picture above shows how the Wave add together to form the interference pattern. 26.6|Shock Waves and Sonic Booms|562
Now we know that the Wave move away from the source at the Speed of Sound What happens if the source moves at the same time as emitting Sound Once Sound Wave has been emitted it is no longer connected to the source so if the source moves it doesnt change the way the Sound Wave is propagating through the medium. This means source can actually catch up with Sound Wave it has emitted. 27|Wave Nature of Matter|571

---------------------------------------------------------

27.1|Introduction|571
In chapters 30 and 31 the so called wave-particle duality if Light is described. This duality states that Light displays properties of both Wave and of particles depending on the experiment performed. For example interference and Diffraction of Light are properties of its Wave nature while the Photoelectric effect is property of its particle nature. In fact we call particle of Light photon. Hopefully you have realised that nature loves symmetry. So if Light which was originally believed to be Wave also has particle nature then perhaps particles also display Wave nature. In other words matter which which we originally thought of as particles may also display wave-particle duality. 
---------------------------------------------------------

27.2|de Broglie Wavelength|571
Einstein showed that for photon its momentum is equal to its Energy divided the Speed of Light c: The Energy of the photon can also be expressed in terms of the Wavelength of the Light hc where is Plancks constant. Combining these two equations we find that the the momentum of the photon is related to its Wavelength hc or equivalently In 1923 Louis de Broglie proposed that this equation not only holds for photons but also holds for particles of matter. This is known as the de Broglie hypothesis Definition: De Broglie Hypothesis particle of Mass moving with Velocity has Wavelength related to is momentum mv by mv (27.1) This Wavelength is known as the de Broglie Wavelength of the particle. Since the value of Plancks constant is incredibly small 6.63 1034 the wavelike nature of everyday objects is not really observable. The de Broglie hypothesis was proposed by French physicist Louis de Broglie (15 August 1892 19 March 1987) in 1923 in his PhD thesis. He was awarded the Nobel Prize for Physics in 1929 for this Work (physics) which made him the first person to receive Nobel Prize on PhD thesis. This Wavelength is considerably smaller than the diameter of proton which is approximately 1015 m. Hence the wave-like properties of this cricket ball are too small to be observed. Although the Electron and cricket ball in the two previous examples are travelling at the same Velocity the de Broglie Wavelength of the Electron is much larger than that of the cricket ball. This is because the Wavelength is inversely proportional to the Mass of the particle. Since the de Broglie Wavelength of particle is inversely proportional to its Velocity the Wavelength decreases as the Velocity increases. This is confirmed in the last two examples with the Electron De Broglies hypothesis was confirmed by Davisson and Germer in 1927 when they observed beam of Electron being Diffraction off nickel surface. The Diffraction means that the moving Electron have Wave nature. They were also able to determine the Wavelength of the Electron from the Diffraction To measure Wavelength one needs two or more diffacting centres such as pinholes slits or atoms. For Diffraction to occur the centres must be separated by Distance about the same size as the Wavelength Theoretically all objects not just sub-atomic particles exhibit Wave properties according to the de Broglie hypothesis. 
---------------------------------------------------------

27.3|The Electron Microscope|574
We have seen that under certain circumstances particles behave like Wave This idea is used in the Electron Optical microscope which is type of Optical microscope that uses Electron to create an image of the target. It has much higher Magnification or resolving Power (physics) than normal Light Optical microscope up to two million times allowing it to see smaller objects and details. Lets first review how regular Optical microscope Work (physics) beam of Light is shone through thin target and the image is then magnified and focused using objective and ocular lenses. The amount of Light which passes through the target depends on the densities of the target since the less dens regions allow more Light to pass through than the denser regions. This means that the beam of Light which is partially transmitted through the target carries information about the inner structure of the target. The original form of the Electron microscopy the transmission Electron microscopy Work (physics) in similar manner using Electron In the Electron Optical microscope Electron which are emitted by cathode are formed into beam using Magnet lenses. This Electron beam is then passed through very thin target. Again the regions in the target with higher densities stop the Electron more easily. So the amount of Electron which pass through the different regions of the target depend their densities. This means that the partially transmitted beam of Electron carries information about the densities of the inner structure of the target. The spatial variation in this information (the image) is then magnified by series of Magnet lenses and it is recorded by hitting fluorescent screen photographic plate or Light sensitive sensor such as CCD (charge-coupled device) camera. The image detected by the CCD may be displayed in real time on monitor or computer. In figure ?? is an image of the polio virus obtained with transmission Electron Optical microscope The structure of an Geometrical optics and Electron Optical microscope are compared in figure 27.3. While the Optical microscope uses Light and focuses using lenses the Electron Optical microscope uses Electron and focuses using electromagnets. The first Electron Optical microscope prototype was built in 1931 by the German engineers Ernst Ruska and Maximillion Knoll. It was based on the ideas and discoveries of Louis de Broglie. Although it was primitive and was not ideal for practical use the instrument was still capable of magnifying objects by four hundred times. The first practical Electron Optical microscope was built at the Electron Optical microscope are very useful as they are able to magnify objects to much higher resolution. This is because their de Broglie Wavelength are so much smaller than that of visible Light You hopefully remember that Light is Diffraction by objects which are separated by Distance of about the same size as the Wavelength of the Light This Diffraction then prevents you from being able to focus the transmitted Light into an image. So the sizes at which Diffraction occurs for beam of Electron is much smaller than those for visible Light This is why you can magnify targets to much higher order of Magnification using Electron rather than visible Light Extension: High-Resolution Transmission Electron Optical microscope (HRTEM) There are high-resolution TEM (HRTEM) which have been built. However their resolution is limited by spherical and chromatic aberration. Fortunately though software correction of the spherical aberration has allowed the production of images with very high resolution. In fact the resolution is sufficient to show carbon atoms in diamond separated by only 89 picometers and atoms in silicon at 78 picometers. This is at Magnification of 50 million times. The ability to determine the Position (vector) of atoms within materials has made the HRTEM very useful tool for nano-technologies research. It is also very important for the development of semiconductor devices for Electron and photonics. Transmission Electron Optical microscope produce two-dimensional images. Extension: Scanning Electron Optical microscope (SEM) The Scanning Electron Optical microscope (SEM) produces images by hitting the target with primary Electron beam which then excites the surface of the target. This causes secondary Electron to be emitted from the surface which are then detected. So the the Electron beam in the SEM is moved across the sample while detectors build an image from the secondary Electron Generally the transmission Electron Optical microscope resolution is about an order of magnitude better than the SEM resolution however because the SEM image relies on surface processes rather than transmission it is able to image bulk samples and has much greater depth of view and so can produce images that are good representation of the 3D structure of the sample. 
---------------------------------------------------------

27.3.1|Disadvantages of an Electron Microscope|577
Electron Optical microscope are expensive to buy and maintain. they are also very sensitive to vibration and external Magnet Field (physics) This means that special facilities are required to house Optical microscope aimed at achieving high resolutions. Also the targets have to be viewed in vacuum as the Electron would Scattering with the molecules that make up air. Extension: Scanning Electron Optical microscope (SEM) Scanning Electron Optical microscope usually image conductive or semi-conductive materials best. common preparation technique is to coat the target with several-nanometer layer of conductive material such as gold from sputtering machine however this process has the potential to disturb delicate samples. The targets have to be prepared in many ways to give proper detail which may result in artifacts purely the result of treatment. This gives the problem of distinguishing artifacts from material particularly in biological samples. Scientists maintain that the results from various preparation techniques have been compared and as there is no reason that they should all produce similar artifacts it is therefore reasonable to believe that Electron microscopy features correlate with living cells. The first Electron Optical microscope prototype was built in 1931 by the German engineers Ernst Ruska and Maximillion Knoll. It was based on the ideas and discoveries of Louis de Broglie. Although it was primitive and was not ideal for practical use the instrument was still capable of magnifying objects by four hundred times. The first practical Electron Optical microscope was built at the University of Toronto in 1938 by Eli Franklin Burton and students Cecil Hall James Hillier and Albert Prebus. Although modern Electron Optical microscope can magnify objects up to two million times they are still based upon Ruskas prototype and his correlation between Wavelength and resolution. The Electron Optical microscope is an integral part of many laboratories. Researchers use it to examine biological materials (such as microorganisms and cells) variety of large molecules medical biopsy samples metals and Crystallinity structures and the characteristics of various surfaces. 
---------------------------------------------------------

27.3.2|Uses of Electron Microscopes|577
Electron Optical microscope can be used to study: the topography of an object how its surface looks. the morphology of particles making up an object its shape and size. the composition of an object the elements and compounds that the object is composed of and the relative amounts of them. the crystallographic information of the object how the atoms are arranged in the object.

28.1|Introduction|579
In Grade 11 you learnt how Magnet Field (physics) is generated around Electric current carrying Electrical conductor You also learnt how Electric current is generated in Electrical conductor that moves in Magnet Field (physics) This chapter describes how Electrical conductor moved in Magnet Field (physics) are applied in the real-world.

28.2|Electrical machines - generators and motors|579
We have seen that when Electrical conductor is moved in Magnet Field (physics) or when Magnet is moved near Electrical conductor such that the Magnet Field (physics) is not parallel to the Electrical conductor Electric current flows in the Electrical conductor The amount of Electric current depends on the Speed at which the Electrical conductor experiences changing Magnet Field (physics) the number of turns of the Electrical conductor and the orientation of the plane of the Electrical conductor with respect to the Magnet Field (physics) The effect of the orientation of the Electrical conductor with respect to the Magnet Field (physics) is shown in Figure 28.1. Figure 28.1: Series of figures showing that the Magnet flux through Electrical conductor is dependent on the angle that the plane of the Electrical conductor makes with the Magnet Field (physics) The greatest flux passes through the Electrical conductor when the plane of the Electrical conductor is perpendicular to the Magnet Field (physics) lines as in (a). The number of Field (physics) lines passing through the Electrical conductor decreases as the Electrical conductor rotates until it is parallel to the Magnet Field (physics) If the Electric current flowing in the Electrical conductor were plotted as function of the angle between the plane of the Electrical conductor and the Magnet Field (physics) then the Electric current would vary as shown in Figure 28.2. The Electric current alternates about the zero value and is also known as an alternating Electric current (abbreviated AC). Figure 28.2: Variation of Electric current as angle of plane of Electrical conductor with the Magnet Field (physics) changes.

28.2.1|Electrical generators|580
AC generator The principle of rotating Electrical conductor in Magnet Field (physics) is used in electricity generators. generator converts Mechanical energy into electrical Energy Definition: Generator generator converts Mechanical energy into electrical Energy The layout of an AC generator is shown in Figure 28.3. The Electrical conductor in the shape of coil is connected to ring. The Electrical conductor is then manually rotated in the Magnet Field (physics) generating an alternating Electromotive force The slip rings are connected to the load via brushes. If machine is constructed to rotate Magnet Field (physics) around set of stationary wire coils with the turning of shaft AC Voltage will be produced across the wire coils as that shaft is rotated in accordance with Faradays Law of electromagnetic induction. This is the basic operating principle of an AC generator. In an AC generator the two ends of the coil are each attached to slip ring that makes contact with brushes as the coil turns. The Direction (geometry) of the Electric current changes with every half turn of the coil. As one side of the loop moves to the other pole of the Magnet Field (physics) the Electric current in it changes Direction (geometry) The two slip rings of the AC generator allow the Electric current to change Direction (geometry) and become alternating Electric current AC generators are also known as alternators. They are found in motor cars to Electric charge the car battery. DC generator DC generator is constructed the same way as an AC generator except that there is one slip ring which is split into two pieces called commutator so the Electric current in the external circuit does not change Direction (geometry) The layout of DC generator is shown in Figure 28.4. The split-ring commutator accommodates for the change in Direction (geometry) of the Electric current in the loop thus creating DC Electric current going through the brushes and out to the circuit. The shape of the Electromotive force from DC generator is shown in Figure 28.5. The Electromotive force is not steady but is more or less the Position (vector) halves of sine Wave AC versus DC generators The problems involved with making and breaking electrical contact with moving coil should be obvious (sparking and heat) especially if the shaft of the generator is revolving at high Speed If the atmosphere surrounding the machine contains flammable or explosive vapors the practical problems of spark-producing brush contacts are even greater. An AC generator (alternator) does not require brushes and commutators to Work (physics) and so is immune to these problems experienced by DC generators. The benefits of AC over DC with regard to generator design is also Reflection (physics) in electric motors. While DC motors require the use of brushes to make electrical contact with moving coils of wire AC motors do not. In fact AC and DC motor designs are very similar to their generator counterparts. The AC motor being dependent upon the reversing Magnet Field (physics) produced by alternating Electric current through its stationary coils of wire to rotate the rotating Magnet around on its shaft and the DC motor being dependent on the brush contacts making and breaking connections to reverse Electric current through the rotating coil every 12 rotation (180 degrees). 
---------------------------------------------------------

28.2.2|Electric motors|582
The basic principles of operation for motor are the same as that of generator except that motor converts electrical Energy into Mechanical energy Definition: Motor An electric motor converts electrical Energy into Mechanical energy Both motors and generators can be explained in terms of coil that rotates in Magnet Field (physics) In generator the coil is attached to an external circuit and it is mechanically turned resulting in changing flux that induces an Electromotive force In motor current-carrying coil in Magnet Field (physics) experiences Force on both sides of the coil creating Torque which makes it turn. Any coil carrying Electric current can feel Force in Magnet Field (physics) the Force is the Lorentz Force on the moving Electric charge in the Electrical conductor We know that if the coil is parallel to the Magnet Field (physics) then the Lorentz Force will be zero. The Electric charge of opposite sides of the coil will be in opposite Direction (geometry) because the Electric charge are moving in opposite Direction (geometry) This means the coil will rotate. Instead of rotating the loops through Magnet Field (physics) to create electricity Electric current is sent through the wires creating electromagnets. The outer Magnet will then repel the electromagnets and rotate the shaft as an electric motor. If the Electric current is AC the two slip rings are required to create an AC motor. An AC motor is shown in Figure 28.6 If the Electric current is DC split-ring commutators are required to create DC motor. This is shown in Figure 28.7.

Cars car contains an alternator that Electric charge up its battery Power (physics) the cars electric system when its engine is running. Alternators have the great advantage over direct-current generators of not using commutator which makes them simpler lighter less costly and more rugged than DC generator. car also contains DC electric motor the starter motor to turn over the engine to start it. starter consists of the very Power (physics) DC electric motor and starter solenoid that is attached to the motor. starter motor requires very high Electric current to crank the engine thats why its connected to the battery with large cables. 28.3|Alternating Current|585
Most students of electricity begin their study with what is known as Direction (geometry) Electric current (DC) which is electricity flowing in constant Direction (geometry) DC is the kind of electricity made by battery with definite Position (vector) and negative terminals). However we have seen that the electricity produced by generator alternates and is therefore known as alternating current(AC). The main advantage to AC is that the Voltage can be changed using transformers. That means that the Voltage can be stepped up at Power (physics) stations to very high Voltage so that electrical Energy can be transmitted along Power (physics) lines at low Electric current and therefore experience low Energy loss due to heating. The Voltage can then be stepped down for use in buildings and street Light In South Africa alternating Electric current is generated at Frequency of 50 Hertz The circuit symbol for alternating Electric current is: Graphs of Voltage against time and Electric current against time for an AC circuit are shown in Figure 28.9 In DC circuit the Electric current and Voltage are constant. In an AC circuit the Electric current and Voltage vary with time. This average value we use for AC is known as the root mean square (rms) average. This is defined as: Since AC varies sinusoidally with as much Position (vector) as negative doing straight average would get you zero for the average Voltage The rms value by-passes this problem.

28.4.1|Capacitance|586

The reactance of Capacitor XC is defined as: XC 2fC where is the Capacitance and is the AC Frequency If we examine the equation for the reactance of Capacitor we see that the Frequency is in the denominator. Therefore when the Frequency is low the Capacitance reactance is very high. This is why Capacitor blocks the flow of DC and low Frequency AC because its reactance increases with decreasing Frequency When the Frequency is high the Capacitance reactance is low. This is why Capacitor allows the flow of high Frequency AC because its reactance decreases with increasing Frequency

28.4.2|Inductance|586
An inductor is passive electrical device used in electrical circuits for its property of inductance. Electrical Electric current through the Electrical conductor creates Magnet flux proportional to the Electric current change in this Electric current creates change in Magnet flux that in turn generates an Electromotive force that acts to oppose this change in Electric current Inductance (measured in henries symbol H) is measure of the generated Electromotive force for unit change in Electric current For example an inductor with an inductance of produces an Electromotive force of when the Electric current through the inductor changes at the rate of As1. The inductance of an inductor is determined by several factors: the shape of the coil short fat coil has higher inductance than one that is thin and tall. the material that Electrical conductor is wrapped around. how the Electrical conductor is wound winding in opposite Direction (geometry) will cancel out the inductance effect and you will have only resistor. The inductance of solenoid is defined by: 0AN2 where is the permeability of the core material (in this case air) is the cross-sectional area of the solenoid is the number of turns and is the Length of the solenoid. Definition: Permeability Permeability is the property of material which describes the magnetisation developed in that material when excited by source. The permeability of free space is 4x107 henry per Metre An inductor in an AC circuit also has reactance XL that is defined by: XL 2fL where is the inductance and is the Frequency of the AC. If we examine the equation for the reactance of an inductor we see that inductive reactance increases with increasing Frequency Therefore when the Frequency is low the inductive reactance is very low. This is why an inductor allows the flow of DC and low Frequency AC because its reactance decreases with decreasing Frequency When the Frequency is high the inductive reactance is high. This is why an inductor blocks the flow of high Frequency AC because its reactance increases with increasing Frequency

29.2|Capacitive and Inductive Circuits|591
Earlier in Grade 12 you were shown alternating Electric current (a.c.) and you saw that the Voltage and the Electric current varied with time. If the a.c. supply is connected to resistor then the Electric current and Voltage will be proportional to each other. This means that the Electric current and Voltage will peak at the same time. We say that the Electric current and Voltage are in phase. This is shown in Figure 29.1. When Capacitor is connected to an alternating Voltage the maximum Voltage is proportional to the maximum Electric current but the maximum Voltage does not occur at the same time as the maximum Electric current The Electric current has its maximum (it peaks) one quarter of cycle before the Voltage peaks. Engineers say that the Electric current leads the Voltage by 90. This is shown in Figure 29.2. For circuit with Capacitor the instantaneous value of is not constant. However the value of Vmax Imax is useful and is called the Capacitance reactance (XC) of the component. Because it is still Voltage divided by Electric current (like Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance its unit is the Ohm The value of XC (C Inductors are very similar but the Electric current peaks 90 after the Voltage This is shown in Figure 29.3. Engineers say that the Electric current lags the Voltage Again the ratio of maximum Voltage to maximum Electric current is called the reactance this time inductive reactance (XL). The value of the reactance depends on its inductance (L). Definition: Reactance The ratio of the maximum Voltage to the maximum Electric current when Capacitor or inductor is connected to an alternating Voltage The unit of reactance is the Ohm While inductive and Capacitance reactances are similar in one sense they are opposites. For an inductor the Electric current peaks 90 after the Voltage For Capacitor the Electric current peaks 90 ahead of the Voltage When we Work (physics) out the total reactance for an inductor and Capacitor in series we use the formula to take this into account. This formula can also be used when there is more than one inductor or more than one Capacitor in the circuit. The total reactance is the sum of all of the inductive reactances minus the sum of all the Capacitance reactances. The magnitude (number) in the final result gives the ratio of maximum Voltage to maximum Electric current in the circuit as whole. The sign of the final result tells you its phase. If it is Position (vector) the Electric current peaks 90 after the Voltage if it is negative the Electric current peaks 90 before the Voltage If Series and parallel circuits contains resistors as well then the situation is more complicated. The maximum Electric current is still proportional to the maximum Voltage but the phase difference between them wont be 90. The ratio between the maximum Voltage and maximum Electric current is called the impedance (Z) and its unit is also the Ohm Impedances are calculated using this formula: X2 R2 (29.4) where is the total reactance of the inductors and Capacitor in the circuit and is the total Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of the resistors in the circuit. It is easier to understand this formula by thinking of right angled triangle. Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance are drawn horizontally reactances are drawn vertically. The hypotenuse of the triangle gives the impedance. This is shown in Figure 29.4. Definition: Impedance The maximum Voltage divided by the maximum Electric current for any circuit. The unit of impedance is the Ohm It is important to remember that when resistors and inductances (or Capacitor are in circuit the Electric current will not be in phase with the Voltage so the impedance is not Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance Similarly the Electric current wont be exactly 90 out of phase with the Voltage so the impedance isnt reactance either. Most factories containing heavy duty electrical equipment (e.g. large motors) have to pay extra money to their electricity supply company because the inductance of the motor coils causes the Electric current and Voltage to get out of phase. As this makes the electricity distribution network less efficient financial penalty is incurred. The factory engineer can prevent this by connecting Capacitor into the circuit to reduce the reactance to zero as in the last question above. The Electric current and Voltage are then in phase again. We cant calculate the Capacitance needed in this chapter because the Capacitor are usually connected in parallel and we have only covered the reactances and impedances of Series and parallel circuits

29.3|Filters and Signal Tuning|596

---------------------------------------------------------

29.3.1|Capacitors and Inductors as Filters|596
We have already seen how Capacitor and inductors pass Electric current more easily at certain Frequency than others. To recap: if we examine the equation for the reactance of Capacitor we see that the Frequency is in the denominator. Therefore when the Frequency is low the Capacitance reactance is very high. This is why Capacitor blocks the flow of DC and low Frequency AC because its reactance increases with decreasing Frequency When the Frequency is high the Capacitance reactance is low. This is why Capacitor allows the flow of high Frequency AC because its reactance decreases with increasing Frequency Therefore putting Capacitor in circuit blocks the low Frequency and allows the high Frequency to pass. This is called high pass filter. filter like this can be used in the treble setting of Sound mixer or music player which controls the amount of high Frequency signal reaching the speaker. The more high Frequency signal there is the tinnier the Sound simple high pass filter circuit is shown in Figure 29.5. Similarly if we examine the equation for the reactance of an inductor we see that inductive reactance increases with increasing Frequency Therefore when the Frequency is low the inductive reactance is very low. This is why an inductor allows the flow of DC and low Frequency AC because its reactance decreases with decreasing Frequency When the Frequency is high the inductive reactance is high. This is why an inductor blocks the flow of high Frequency AC because its reactance increases with increasing Frequency Therefore putting an inductor in circuit blocks the high Frequency and allows the low Frequency to pass. This is called low pass filter. filter like this can be used in the bass setting of Sound mixer or music player which controls the amount of low Frequency signal reaching the speaker. The more low Frequency signal there is the more the Sound booms. simple low pass filter circuit is shown in Figure 29.6. Figure 29.5: high pass filter. High Frequency easily pass through the Capacitor and into the next part of the circuit while low Frequency pass through the inductor straight to ground. 
---------------------------------------------------------

29.3.2|LRC Circuits, Resonance and Signal Tuning|596
circuit containing resistor Capacitor and an inductor all in series is called an LRC circuit. Because the components are in series the Electric current through each component at particular time will be the same as the Electric current through the others. The Voltage across the resistor will be in phase with the Electric current The Voltage across the inductor will be 90 ahead of the Electric current (the Electric current always follows or lags the Voltage in an inductor). The Voltage across the Capacitor will be 90 behind the Electric current (the Electric current leads the Voltage for Capacitor The phases of the three Voltage are shown in Figure 29.7. Figure 29.6: low pass filter. Low Frequency pass through the inductor and into the next part of the circuit while high Frequency pass through the Capacitor straight to ground. Figure 29.7: The Voltage across the separate components of an LRC circuit. Looking at the peaks you see that the Voltage across the inductor VL peaks first followed 90 later by the Electric current followed 90 later by the Voltage across the Capacitor VC. The Voltage across the resistor is not shown it is in phase with the Electric current and peaks at the same time as the Electric current 59 The reactance of the inductor is 2fL and the reactance of the Capacitor is 12fC but with the opposite phase. So the total reactance of the LRC circuit is XL XC 2fL 2fC The impedance of the circuit as whole is given by X2 R2 2fL 2fC R2 At different Frequency the impedance will take different values. The impedance will have its smallest value when the Position (vector) inductive reactance cancels out the negative Capacitance reactance. This occurs when 2fL 2fC so the Frequency of minimum impedance must be 2LC This is called the Resonance (particle physics) Frequency of the circuit. This is the Frequency at which you can get the largest Electric current for particular supply Voltage It is also called the natural Frequency of the circuit. This means the Frequency at which the circuit would oscillate by itself. Definition: Resonance (particle physics) Resonance (particle physics) occurs when circuit is connected to an alternating Voltage at its natural fre- quency. very large Electric current in the circuit can build up even with minimal Power (physics) input. An LRC circuit is very useful when we have signal containing many different Frequency and we only want one of them. If signal like this is connected to an LRC circuit then only the Resonance (particle physics) Frequency (and other Frequency close to it) will drive measureable Electric current This means that an LRC circuit can select one Frequency from range. This process is called signal tuning. When you set up radio antenna and amplify the radio signal it receives you find many different bands of Frequency one from each radio station. When you listen to the radio you only want to listen to one station. An LRC circuit in the radio (the tuning circuit) is set so that its Resonance (particle physics) Frequency is the Frequency of the station you want to listen to. This means that of the many radio stations broadcasting you only hear one. When you adjust the tuning dial on the radio it changes the Capacitance of the Capacitor in the tuning circuit. This changes the Resonance (particle physics) Frequency and this changes the radio station that you will hear.

29.4|Active Circuit Elements|599
The components you have been learning about so far resistors Capacitor and inductors are called passive components. They do not change their behaviour or Physics in response to changes in Voltage or Electric current Active components are quite different. Their response to changes in input allows them to make amplifiers calculators and computers. 
---------------------------------------------------------

29.4.1|The Diode|599
diode is an Electron device that allows Electric current to flow in one Direction (geometry) only. diode consists of two doped semi-conductors joined together so that the Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance is low when connected one way and very high the other way. Figure 29.9: Operation of diode. (a) The diode is forward biased and Electric current is permitted. The negative terminal of the battery is connected to the negative terminal of the diode. (b) The diode is reverse biased and Electric current flow is not allowed. The negative terminal of the battery is connected to the Position (vector) terminal of the diode. full explanation of diode operation is complex. Here is simplified description. The diode consists of two semiconductor blocks attached together. Neither block is made of pure silicon they are both doped. Doping was described in more detail in Section 10.3. In short p-type semiconductor has fewer free Electron than normal semiconductor. stands for Position (vector) meaning lack of Electron although the material is actually neutral. The locations where Electron are missing are called holes. This material can conduct electricity well because Electron can move into the holes making new hole somewhere else in the material. Any extra Electron introduced into this region by the circuit will fill some or all of the holes. In n-type semiconductor the situation is reversed. The material has an more free Electron than normal semiconductor. stands for negative meaning an excess of Electron although the material is actually neutral. When p-type semiconductor is attached to an n-type semiconductor some of the free Electron in the n-type move across to the p-type semiconductor. They fill the available holes near the junction. This means that the region of the n-type semiconductor nearest the junction has no free Electron (theyve moved across to fill the holes). This makes this n-type semiconductor Position (vector) Electric charge It used to be Electric charge but has since lost Electron The region of p-type semiconductor nearest the junction now has no holes (theyve been filled in by the migrating Electron This makes the p-type semiconductor Electric charge It used to be Electric charge but has since gained Electron Without free Electron or holes the central region can not conduct electricity well. It has high Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance and is called the depletion band. This is shown in Figure 29.10. You can explain the high Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance in different way. free Electron in the n-type semiconductor will be repelled from the p-type semiconductor because of its Electric charge The Electron will not go into the depletion band and certainly wont cross the band to the p-type semiconductor. You may ask But wont free Electron in the p-type semiconductor be attracted across the band carrying Electric current But there are no free Electron in p-type semiconductor so no Electric current of this kind can flow. If the diode is reverse-biased the terminal of the battery is connected to the n-type semiconductor. This makes it even more Electric charge It also removes even more of the free Electron near the depletion band. At the same time the terminal of the battery is connected to the p-type silicon. This will supply free Electron and fill in more of the holes next to the depletion band. Both processes cause the depletion band to get wider. The Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of the diode (which was already high) increases. This is why reverse-biased diode does not conduct. Another explanation for the increased Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance is that the battery has made the p-type semiconductor more negative than it used to be making it repel any Electron from the n-type semiconductor which attempt to cross the depletion band. On the other hand if the diode is forward biased the depletion band is made narrower. The Electric charge on the p-type silicon is cancelled out by the battery. The greater the Voltage used the narrower the depletion band becomes. Eventually when the Voltage is about 06 (for silicon) the depletion band disappears. Once this has occurred the diode conducts very well. Figure 29.10: diode consists of two doped semi-conductors joined together so that the resis- tance is low when connected one way and very high the other way. 
---------------------------------------------------------

29.4.2|The Light Emitting Diode (LED)|601
light-emitting diode (LED) is diode device that emits Light when Electric charge flows in the correct Direction (geometry) through it. If you apply Voltage to Force Electric current to flow in the Direction (geometry) the LED allows it will Light up. Extension: Circuit Symbols This notation of having two small arrows pointing away from the device is common to the schematic symbols of all light-emitting semiconductor devices. Conversely if device is light-activated (meaning that incoming Light stimulates it) then the symbol will have two small arrows pointing toward it. It is interesting to note though that LEDs are capable of acting as light-sensing devices: they will generate small Voltage when exposed to Light much like solar cell on small scale. This property can be gainfully applied in variety of light-sensing circuits. The Color depends on the semiconducting material used to construct the LED and can be in the near-ultraviolet visible or infrared part of the Electromagnetic spectrum Nick Holonyak Jr. (1928 of the University of Illinois at Urbana-Champaign developed the first practical visible-spectrum LED in 1962. Light Emission spectrum The Wavelength of the Light emitted and therefore its Color depends on the materials forming the p-n junction. normal diode typically made of silicon or germanium emits invisible far-infrared Light (so it cant be seen) but the materials used for an LED have emit Light corresponding to near-infrared visible or near-ultraviolet Frequency LED applications LEDs have many uses. Some of these are given here. thin lightweight message displays e.g. in public information signs (at airports and railway stations among other places) status indicators e.g. onoff Light on professional instruments and consumers audiovideo equipment infrared LEDs in remote controls (for TVs VCRs etc) clusters of LEDs are used in traffic signals replacing ordinary bulbs behind Color glass car indicator Light and bicycle Light calculator and measurement instrument displays (seven segment displays) although now mostly replaced by LCDs red or yellow LEDs are used in indicator and alphanumeric displays in environments where night vision must be retained: aircraft cockpits submarine and ship bridges astronomy observatories and in the Field (physics) e.g. night time animal watching and military Field (physics) use red or yellow LEDs are also used in photographic darkrooms for providing Light which does not lead to unwanted exposure of the film illumination e.g. flashlights (a.k.a. torches UK) and backlighting for LCD screens signalingemergency beacons and strobes movement sensors e.g. in mechanical and Geometrical optics computer mice and trackballs in LED printers e.g. high-end Color printers LEDs offer benefits in terms of maintenance and safety. The typical Work (physics) lifetime of device including the bulb is ten years which is much longer than the lifetimes of most other Light sources. LEDs fail by dimming over time rather than the abrupt burn-out of incandescent bulbs. LEDs give off less heat than incandescent Light bulbs and are less fragile than fluorescent lamps. Since an individual device is smaller than centimetre in Length LED-based Light sources used for illumination and outdoor signals are built using clusters of tens of devices. Because they are monochromatic LED Light have great Power (physics) advantages over white Light where specific Color is required. Unlike the white Light the LED does not need filter that absorbs most of the emitted white Light Color fluorescent Light are made but they are not widely available. LED Light are inherently Color and are available in wide range of Color One of the most recently introduced Color is the emerald green (bluish green about 500 nm) that meets the legal requirements for traffic signals and navigation Light There are applications that specifically require Light that does not contain any blue component. Examples are photographic darkroom safe Light illumination in laboratories where certain photo-sensitive chemicals are used and situations where dark adaptation (night vision) must be preserved such as cockpit and bridge illumination observatories etc. Yellow LED Light are good choice to meet these special requirements because the human eye is more sensitive to yellow Light
