29.4.3|Transistor|603
The diode is the simplest semiconductor device made up of p-type semiconductor and an n-type semiconductor in contact. It can conduct in only one Direction (geometry) but it cannot control the size of an electric Electric current Transistors are more complicated Electron components which can control the size of the electric Electric current flowing through them. This enables them to be used in amplifiers. small signal from microphone or radio antenna can be used to control the transistor. In response the transistor will then increase and decrease much larger Electric current which flows through the speakers. One of the earliest popular uses of transistors was in cheap and portable radios. Before that radios were much more expensive and contained glass valves which were fragile and needed replacing. In some parts of the world you can still hear people talking about their transistor they mean their portable radio. You can also use small Electric current to turn the transistor on and off. The transistor then controls more complicated or Power (physics) Electric current through other components. When transistor is used in this way it is said to be in switching mode as it is acting as remotely controlled switch. As we shall see in the final sections of this chapter switching circuits can be used in computer to process and store digital information. computer would not Work (physics) without the millions (or billions) of transistors in it. There are two main types of transistor bipolar transistors (NPN or PNP) and Field (physics) effect transistors (FETs). Both use doped semiconductors but in different ways. You are mainly required to know about Field (physics) effect transistors (FETs) however we have to give brief description of bipolar transistors so that you see the difference. Bipolar Transistors Bipolar transistors are made of doped semiconductor sandwich. In an NPN transistor very thin layer of p-type semiconductor is in between two thicker layers of n-type semiconductor. This is shown in Figure 29.11. Similarly an PNP transistor consists of very thin n-type layer in between two thicker layers of p-type semiconductor. In an NPN transistor small Electric current of Electron flows from the emitter (E) to the base (B). Simultaneously much larger Electric current of Electron flows from the emitter (E) to the collector (C). If you lower the number of Electron able to leave the transistor at the base (B) the transistor automatically reduces the number of Electron flowing from emitter (E) to collector (C). Similarly if you increase the Electric current of Electron flowing out of the base (B) the transistor automatically also increases the Electric current of Electron flowing from emitter (E) to collector (C). The transistor is designed so that the Electric current of Electron from emitter to collector (IEC) is proportional to the Electric current of Electron from emitter to base (IEB). The constant of proportionality is known as the Electric current gain So IEC IEB. How does it do it? The answer comes from our Work (physics) with diodes. Electron arriving at the emitter (n-type semiconductor) will naturally flow through into the central p-type since the base-emitter junction is forward biased. However if none of these Electron are removed from the base the Electron flowing into the base from the emitter will fill all of the available holes. Accordingly large depletion band will be set up. This will act as an Insulator (electricity) preventing Electric current flow into the collector as well. On the other hand if the base is connected to Position (vector) Voltage small number of Electron will be removed by the base connection. This will prevent the holes in the base becoming filled up and no depletion band will form. While some Electron from the emitter leave via the base connection the bulk of them flow straight on to the collector. You may wonder how the Electron get from the base into the collector (it seems to be reverse biased). The answer is complicated but the important fact is that the p-type layer is extremely thin. As long as there is no depletion layer the bulk of the Electron will have no difficulty passing straight from the n-type emitter into the n-type collector. more satisfactory answer can be given to university student once band theory has been explained. Summing up in an NPN transistor small flow of Electron from emitter (E) to base (B) allows much larger flow of Electron from emitter (E) to collector (C). Given that conventional Electric current (flowing from to is in the opposite Direction (geometry) to Electron flow we say that small conventional Electric current from base to emitter allows large Electric current to flow from collector to emitter. PNP transistor Work (physics) the other way. small conventional Electric current from emitter to base allows much larger conventional Electric current to flow from emitter to collector. The operation is more complicated to explain since the principal Electric charge carrier in PNP transistor is not the Electron but the hole. The operation of NPN and PNP transistors (in terms of conventional Electric current is summarized in Figure 29.12. The transistor is considered by many to be one of the greatest discoveries or inventions in modern history ranking with banking and the printing press. Key to the importance of the transistor in modern society is its ability to be produced in huge numbers using simple techniques resulting in vanishingly small prices. Computer chips consist of millions of transistors and sell for Rands with per-transistor costs in the thousandths-of-cents. The low cost has meant that the transistor has become an almost universal tool for non-mechanical tasks. Whereas common device say refrigerator would have used mechanical device for control today it is often less expensive to simply use few million transistors and the appropriate computer program to carry out the same task through brute Force Today transistors have replaced almost all electromechanical devices most simple feedback systems and appear in huge numbers in everything from computers to cars. The transistor was invented at Bell Laboratories in December 1947 (first demonstrated on December 23) by John Bardeen Walter Houser Brattain and William Bradford Shockley who were awarded the Nobel Prize in Physics in 1956. The Field (physics) Effect Transistor (FET) To control bipolar transistors you control the Electric current flowing into or out of its base. The other type of transistor is the Field (physics) effect transistor (FET). FETs Work (physics) using control Voltage instead. Accordingly they can be controlled with much smaller Electric current and are much more economic to use. No-one would build computer with billions of bipolar transistors the Electric current in each transistors base might be small but when you add up all of the base Electric current in the millions of transistors the computer as whole would be consuming great deal of electricity and making great deal of heat. Not only is this wasteful it would prevent manufacturers making computer of convenient size. If the transistors were too close together they would overheat. Figure 29.13: Field (physics) effect transistor (FET). The diagram on the left shows the semiconductor structure. The diagram on the right shows its circuit symbol. The three terminals of the FET are called the source (S) drain (D) and gate (G) as shown in Figure 29.13. When the gate is not connected Electric current of Electron can flow from source (S) to drain (D) easily along the channel. The source is accordingly the negative terminal of the transistor. The drain where the Electron come out is the Position (vector) terminal of the transistor. few Electron will flow from the n-type channel into the p-type semiconductor of the gate when the device is manufactured. However as these Electron are not removed (the gate is not connected) depletion band is set up which prevents further flow into the gate. In operation the gate is connected to negative Voltage relative to the source. This makes the p-n junction between gate and channel reverse-biased. Accordingly no Electric current flows from the source into the gate. When the Voltage of the gate is lowered (made more negative) the depletion band becomes wider. This enlarged depletion band takes up some of the space of the channel. So the lower the Voltage of the gate (the more negative it is relative to the source) the larger the depletion band. The larger the depletion band the narrower the channel. The narrower the channel the harder it is for Electron to flow from source to drain. The Voltage of the gate is not the only factor affecting the Electric current of Electron between the source and the drain. If the external circuit has low Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance Electron are able to leave the drain easily. If the external circuit has high Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance Electron leave the drain slowly. This creates kind of traffic jam which slows the passage of further Electron In this way the Voltage of the drain regulates itself and is more or less independent of the Electric current demanded from the drain. Once these two factors have been taken into account it is fair to say that the Position (vector) output Voltage (the Voltage of the drain relative to the source) is proportional to the negative input Voltage (the Voltage of the gate relative to the source). For this reason the Field (physics) effect transistor is known as Voltage amplifier. This contrasts with the bipolar transistor which is Electric current amplifier. 
---------------------------------------------------------

29.4.4|The Operational Amplifier|607
The operational amplifier is special kind of Voltage amplifier which is made from handful of bipolar or Field (physics) effect transistors. Operational amplifiers are usually called op-amps for short. They are used extensively in all kinds of audio equipment (amplifiers mixers and so on) and in instrumentation. They also have many other uses in other circuit for example comparing Voltage from sensors. Operational amplifiers are supplied on Integrated Circuits (I.C.s). The most famous operational amplifier I.C. is numbered 741 and contains single operational amplifier on an integrated circuit (chip) with eight terminals. Other varieties can be bought and you can get single integrated circuit with two or four 741-type operational amplifiers on it. The symbol for an op-amp is shown in Figure 29.14. The operational amplifier has two input terminals and one output terminal. The Voltage of the output terminal is proportional to the difference in Voltage between the two input terminals. The output terminal is on the right (at the sharp point of the triangle). The two input terminals are drawn on the left. One input terminal (labelled with on diagrams) is called the non-inverting input. The other input terminal (labelled is called the inverting input. The labels and have nothing to do with the way in which the operational amplifier is connected to the Power (physics) supply. Operational amplifiers must be connected to the Power (physics) supply but this is taken for granted when circuit diagrams are drawn and these connections are not shown on circuit diagrams. Usually when drawing Electron circuits 0V is taken to mean the negative terminal of the Power (physics) supply. This is not the case with op-amps. For an op-amp 0V refers to the Voltage midway between the and of the supply. The output Voltage of the amplifier Vout is given by the formula here is constant called the open loop gain and V+ and are the Voltage of the two input terminals. That said the output Voltage can not be less than the Voltage of the negative terminal of the battery supplying it or higher than the Position (vector) terminal of the battery supplying it. You will notice that Vout is Position (vector) if V+ and negative if V+ V. This is why the input is called the inverting input: raising its Voltage causes the output Voltage to drop. The input Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of an operational amplifier is very high. This means that very little Electric current flows into the input terminals during operation. If all of the transistors in the operational amplifier were identical then the output Voltage would be zero if the two inputs were at equal Voltage In practice this is not quite the case and for sensitive Work (physics) trimming potentiometer is connected. This is adjusted until the op-amp is zeroed correctly. Simple operational amplifiers require the trimming potentiometer to be built into the circuit containing them and an example is shown in Figure 29.15. Other operational amplifier designs incorporate separate terminals for the trimming potentiometer. These special terminals are labelled offset on the manufacturers diagram. The exact method of connecting the potentiometer to the offset terminals can depend on the design of the operational amplifier and you need to refer to the manufacturers data sheet for details of which potentiometer to use and how to connect it. For most commercially produced operational amplifiers (known as op-amps for short) the open loop gain is very large and does not stay constant. Values of 100 000 are typical. Usually designer would want an amplifier with stable gain of smaller value and builds the operational amplifier into circuit like the one in Figure 29.15. 
---------------------------------------------------------

29.5|The Principles of Digital Electronics|609
The circuits and components we have discussed are very useful. You can build radio or television with them. You can make telephone. Even if that was all there was to Electron it would still be very useful. However the great breakthrough in the last fifty years or so has been in digital Electron This is the subject which gave us the computer. The computer has revolutionized the way business engineering and science are done. Small computers programmed to do specific job (called microprocessors) are now used in almost every Electron machine from cars to washing machines. Computers have also changed the way we communicate. We used to have telegraph or telephone wires passing up and down country each one carrying one telephone call or signal. We now have Geometrical optics fibres each capable of carrying tens of thousands of telephone calls using digital signals. So what is digital signal? Look at Figure 29.16. normal signal called an analogue signal carries smooth Wave At any time the Voltage of the signal could take any value. It could be 200 or 353 or anything else. digital signal can only take certain Voltage The simplest case is shown in the figure the Voltage takes one of two values. It is either high or it is low. It never has any other value. These two special Voltage are given symbols. The low Voltage level is written while the high Voltage level is written as 1. When you send digital signal you set the Voltage you want (0 or 1) then keep this fixed for fixed amount of time (for example 0.01 s) then you send the next or 1. The digital signal in Figure 29.16 could be written 01100101. Why are digital signals so good? Figure 29.16: The difference between normal (analogue) signals and digital signals. The analogue signal is on the left. 1. Using computer any information can be turned into pattern of 0s and 1s. Pictures recorded music text and Motion pictures can all be turned into string of 0s and 1s and transmitted or stored in the same way. The computer receiving the signal at the other end converts it back again. Compact Disc (CD) for example can store music or text or pictures and all can be read using computer. 2. The and the look very different. You can immediately tell if or is being sent. Even if there is interference you can still tell whether the sender sent or 1. This means that fewer mistakes are made when reading digital signal. This is why the best music recording technologies and the most modern cameras for example all use digital technology. 3. Using the 0s and 1s you can count and do all kinds of mathematics. This will be explained in more detail in the next section. The simplest digital circuits are called logic gates. Each logic gate makes decision based on the information it receives. Different logic gates are set up to make the decisions in different ways. Each logic gate will be made of many Optical microscope transistors connected together within thin wafer of silicon. This tiny circuit is called an Integrated Circuit or I.C. all the parts are in one place (integrated) on the silicon wafer. 
---------------------------------------------------------

29.5.1|Logic Gates|610
There are five main types of logic gate: NOT AND OR NAND and NOR. Each one makes its decision in different way. The NOT Gate Problem: You want an automatic circuit in your office to turn on the heating in the winter. You already have digital Electron Temperature sensor. When the Temperature is high it sends out 1. When the office is cold it sends out 0. If this signal were sent straight to the heater the heater would turn on (1) when it was already hot and would stay off when it was cold. This is wrong To make the heater Work (physics) we need circuit which will change (from the sensor) into (to send to the heater). This will make the heater come on when it is cold. You also want it to change (from the sensor) into (to send to the heater). This will turn the heater off when the room is hot. This circuit is called an inverter or NOT gate. It changes into (1 is NOT 0). It changes into (0 is NOT 1). It changes signal into what it is NOT. The symbol for the NOT gate is: The action of the NOT gate is written in table called truth table. The left column shows the possible inputs on different rows. The right column shows what the output (decision) of the circuit will be for that input. The truth table for the NOT gate is shown below. When you read the truth table the top row says If the input is the output will be 1. For our heater this means If the room is cold the heater will turn on. The bottom row says If the input is the output will be 0. For our heater this means If the room is hot the heater will switch off. The AND Gate Problem: An airliner has two toilets. Passengers get annoyed if they get up from their seat only to find that both toilets are being used and they have to go back to their seat and wait. You want to fit an automatic circuit to Light up display if both toilets are in use. Then passengers know that if the Light is off there will be free toilet for them to use. There is sensor in each toilet. It gives out of the toilet is free and if it is in use. You want to send to the display unit if both sensors are sending 1s. To do this you use an AND gate. The symbol for the AND gate is: The truth table for the AND gate is shown below. An AND gate has two inputs (the NOT gate only had one). This means we need four rows in the truth table one for each possible set of inputs. The first row for example tells us what the AND gate will do if both inputs are 0. In our airliner this means that both toilets are free. The right column has showing that the output will be so the display will not Light up. The second row has inputs of and (the first toilet is free the other is in use). Again the output is 0. The third row tells us what will happen if the inputs are and (the first toilet is in use and the second is free). Finally the last line tells us what will happen if both inputs are (both toilets are in use). It is only in this case that the output is and the display Light up. This device is called an AND gate because the output is only if one input AND the other input are both 1. Extension: Using and to mean True and False When we use logic gates we use the low Voltage state to represent false. The high Voltage state represents true. This is why the word AND is so appropriate. AND is true (1) if and only if is true (1) AND is true (1). Extension: AND and multiplication Sometimes the AND operation is written as multiplication. AND is written AB. If either or are then AB will also be 0. For AB to be we need and to both be 1. Multiplication of the numbers and does exactly the same job as an AND gate. The NAND Gate Problem: You build the circuit for the airliner toilets using an AND gate. Your customer is pleased but she says that it would be better if the display lit up when there was free toilet. In other words the display should Light up unless both toilets are in use. To do this we want circuit which does the opposite of an AND gate. We want circuit which would give the output if an AND gate would give 1. We want circuit which would give the output if an AND gate would give 0. This circuit is called NAND gate. The symbol for the NAND gate is: You may have noticed that we could have done this job on the airliner by using our earlier circuit with NOT gate added between the original AND gate and the display. This is where the word NAND comes from it is short for NotAND. The OR Gate Problem: long dark corridor has two Light switches one at each end of the corridor. The switches each send an output of to the control unit if no-one has pressed the switch. If someone presses the switch its output is 1. The Light in the corridor should come on if either switch is pressed. To do this job the control unit needs an OR gate. The symbol for the OR gate is: The truth table for the OR gate is shown. You can see that the output is (and the Light come on in the corridor) if either one switch OR the other is pressed. Pressing both switches also turns on the Light as the last row in the table shows. Extension: OR and addition Sometimes you will see OR written mathematically as A+B. This makes sense since if A0 and B0 then OR A+B 0. Similarly if A0 and B1 then OR A+B 1. If A1 and B0 then OR A+B once again. The only case where the OR function differs from normal addition is when A1 and B1. Here OR in logic but A+B2 in arithmetic. However there is no such thing as in logic so we define to mean OR and write 1+11 with impunity If you wish you can prove that the normal rules of algebra still Work (physics) using this notation: A+(B+C) (A+B)+C A(BC) (AB)C and A(B+C) AB AC. This special kind of algebra where variables can only be (representing false) or (representing true) is called Boolean algebra. The NOR Gate The last gate you need to know is the NOR gate. This is opposite to the OR gate. The output is if both inputs are 0. In other words the output switches on if neither the first NOR the second input is 1. The symbol for the NOR gate is: The truth table for the NOR gate is shown below. The examples given were easy. Each job only needed one logic gate. However any decision making circuit can be built with logic gates no matter how complicated the decision. Here is an example. Each logic gate is manufactured from two or more transistors. Other circuits can be made using logic gates as we shall see in the next section. We shall show you how to count and store numbers using logic gates. This means that if you have enough transistors and you connect them correctly to make the right logic gates you can make circuits which count and store numbers. In practice the cheapest gate to manufacture is usually the NAND gate. Additionally Charles Peirce showed that NAND gates alone (as well as NOR gates alone) can be used to reproduce all the other logic gates.

29.6|Using and Storing Binary Numbers|616
In the previous section we saw how the numbers and could represent false and true and could be used in decision making. Often we want to program computer to count with numbers. To do this we need way of writing any number using nothing other than and 1. When written in this way numbers are called binary numbers. Definition: Binary way of writing any number using only the digits and 1. 
---------------------------------------------------------

29.6.1|Binary numbers|616
In normal (denary) numbers we write 9+1 as 10. The fact that the in 10 is the second digit from the right tells us that it actually means 10 and not 1. Similarly the in 365 represents 300 because it is the third digit from the right. You could write 365 as 100 10 5. You will notice the pattern that the nth digit from the right represents 10n1. In binary we use the nth digit from the right to represent 2n1. Thus is written as 10 in binary. Similarly 22 is written as 100 in binary and 23 is written as 1000 in binary. How do you write numbers as sum of Power (physics) of two? The first Power (physics) of two (the largest) is the largest Power (physics) of two which is not larger than the number you are Work (physics) with. In our last example where we wanted to know what twelve was in binary the largest Power (physics) of two which is not larger than 12 is 8. Thus 12 something. By arithmetic the something must be and the largest Power (physics) of two not larger than this is exactly. Thus 12 and we have finished. more complicated example would be to write one hundred in binary. The largest Power (physics) of two not larger than 100 is 64 (1000000 in binary). Subtracting 64 from 100 leaves 36. The largest Power (physics) of two not larger than 36 is 32 (100000 in binary). Removing this leaves remainder of which is Power (physics) of two itself (100 in binary). Thus one hundred is 64 32 or in binary 1000000 100000 100 1100100. Once number is written in binary it can be represented using the low and high Voltage levels of digital Electron We demonstrate how this is done by showing you how an Electron counter Work (physics) 
---------------------------------------------------------

29.6.2|Counting circuits|617
To make counter you need several flip flops sometimes called divide by two circuits. flip flop is digital circuit which swaps its output (from to or from to 0) whenever the input changes from to 0. When the input changes from to it doesnt change its output. It is called flip flop because it changes (flips or flops) each time it receives pulse. If you put series of pulses 10101010 into flip flop the result is 01100110. Figure 29.18 makes this clearer. As you can see from Figure 29.18 there are half as many pulses in the output. This is why it is called divide by two circuit. If we connect flip flops in chain then we make counter which can count pulses. As an example we connect three flip flops in chain. This is shown in Figure 29.19. When this circuit is fed with stream of pulses the outputs of the different stages change. The table below shows how this happens. Each row shows different stage with the first stage at the top. We assume that all of the flip flops have as their output to start with. Figure 29.18: The output of flip flop or divide by two circuit when square Wave is connected to the input. The output changes state when the input goes from to 0. Figure 29.19: Three flip flops connected together in chain to make counter. The input of each flip flop is labelled while each output is labelled Electric charge The pulses are connected to the input on the left. The outputs Electric charge Electric charge and Electric charge give the three digits of the binary number as the pulses are counted. This is explained in the text and in the next table. The binary numbers in the right hand column count the pulses arriving at the input. You will notice that the output of the first flip flop gives the right most digit of the pulse count (in binary). The output of the second flip flop gives the second digit from the right (the twos digit) of the pulse count. The output of the third flip flop gives the third digit from the right (the fours digit) of the pulse count. As there are only three flip flops there is nothing to provide the next digit (the eights digit) and so the eighth pulse is recorded as 000 not 1000. This device is called modulo counter because it can count in eight stages from 000 to 111 before it goes back to 000. If you put four flip flops in the counter it will count in sixteen stages from 0000 to 1111 and it is called modulo 16 counter because it counts in sixteen stages before going back to 0000. Definition: Modulo The modulo of counter tells you how many stages (or pulses) it receives before going back to as its output. Thus modulo counter counts in eight stages 000 001 010 011 100 101 110 111 then returns to 000 again. 
---------------------------------------------------------

29.6.3|Storing binary numbers|619
Counting is important. However it is equally important to be able to remember the numbers. Computers can convert almost anything to string of 0s and 1s and therefore to binary number. Unless this number can be stored in the computers memory the computer would be useless. The memory in the computer contains many parts. Each part is able to store single or 1. Since and are the two binary digits we say that each part of the memory stores one bit. Figure 29.20: bistable circuit made from two NOR gates. This circuit is able to store one bit of digital information. With the two inputs set to you can see that the output could be (and will remain) either or 1. The circuit on the left shows an output of the circuit on the right shows an output of 1. Wires carrying high logic levels (1) are drawn thicker. The output of the bistable is labelled Electric charge Definition: Bit One bit is short way of saying one binary digit. It is single or 1. If you have eight bits you can store binary number from 00000000 to 11111111 (0 to 255 in denary). This gives you enough permutations of 0s and 1s to have one for each letter of the alphabet (in upper and lower case) each digit from to each punctuation mark and each control code used by computer in storing document. When you type text into word processor each character is stored as set of eight bits. Each set of eight bits is called byte. Computer memories are graded according to how many bytes they store. There are 1024 bytes in kilobyte (kB) 1024 1024 bytes in megabyte (MB) and 1024 1024 1024 bytes in gigabyte (GB). To store bit we need circuit which can remember or 1. This is called bistable circuit because it has two stable states. It can stay indefinitely either as or 1. An example of bistable circuit is shown in Figure 29.20. It is made from two NOR gates. To store the or the in the bistable circuit you set one of the inputs to then put it back to again. If the input labelled (set) is raised the output will immediately become 1. This is shown in Figure 29.21. To store you raise the (reset) input to 1. This is shown in Figure 29.22. Once you have used the or inputs to set or reset the bistable circuit you then bring both inputs back to 0. The bistable remembers the state. Because of the ease with which the circuit can be Reset and Set it is also called RS flip flop circuit. computer memory will be able to store millions or billions of bits. If it used our circuit above it would need millions or billions of NOR gates each of which is made from several transistors. The computer memory is made of many millions of transistors. The bistable circuits drawn here dont remember 0s or 1s for ever they lose the information if the Power (physics) is turned off. The same is true for the RAM (Random Access Memory) used to store Work (physics) and temporary data in computer. Some modern circuits contain special memory which can remember its state even if the Power (physics) is turned off. This is used in FLASH drives commonly found in USB data sticks and on the memory cards used with digital cameras. These bistable circuits are much more complex. You can also make flip flops out of logic gates however these are more complicated to design.

30|EM Radiation|625

---------------------------------------------------------

30.1|Introduction|625
This chapter will focus on the electromagnetic Electromagnetic radiation Electromagnetic radiation is self-propagating Wave in space with electric and Magnet components. These components oscillate at right angles to each other and to the Direction (geometry) of propagation and are in phase with each other. Electromagnetic radiation is classified into types according to the Frequency of the Wave these types include in order of increasing Frequency radio Wave microwaves infrared radiation visible Light ultraviolet radiation X-rays and gamma Ray (optics) 
---------------------------------------------------------

30.2|Particle/wave nature of electromagnetic radiation|625
If you watch colony of ants walking up the wall they look like thin continuous black line. But as you look closer you see that the line is made up of thousands of separated black ants. Light and all other types of Electromagnetic radiation seems like continuous Wave at first but when one performs experiments on the Light one can notice that the Light can have both Wave and particle like properties. Just like the individual ants the Light can also be made up of individual bundles of Energy or quanta of Light Light has both wave-like and particle-like properties (waveparticle duality) but only shows one or the other depending on the kind of experiment we perform. wave-type experiment shows the Wave nature and particle-type experiment shows particle nature. One cannot test the Wave and the particle nature at the same time. particle of Light is called photon. Definition: Photon photon is Energy level packet) of Light The particle nature of Light can be demonstrated by the interaction of photons with matter. One way in which Light interacts with matter is via the Photoelectric effect which will be studied in detail in Chapter 31. 
---------------------------------------------------------

30.3|The wave nature of electromagnetic radiation|626
Accelerating Electric charge emit electromagnetic Wave We have seen that changing Electric field generates Magnet Field (physics) and changing Magnet Field (physics) generates an Electric field This is the principle behind the propagation of electromagnetic Wave because electromagnetic Wave unlike Sound Wave do not need medium to travel through. EM Wave propagate when an Electric field oscillating in one plane produces Magnet Field (physics) oscillating in plane at right angles to it which produces an oscillating Electric field and so on. The propagation of electromagnetic Wave can be described as mutual induction. These mutually regenerating Field (physics) travel through space at constant Speed of 108m s1 represented by c. 
---------------------------------------------------------

30.4|Electromagnetic spectrum|626
Observe the things around you your friend sitting next to you large tree across the Field (physics) How is it that you are able to see these things? What is it that is leaving your friends arm and entering your eye so that you can see his arm? It is Light The Light originally comes from the sun or possibly Light bulb or burning fire. In Physics Light is given the more technical term Electromagnetic radiation which includes all forms of Light not just the form which you can see with your eyes. Electromagnetic radiation allows us to observe the world around us. It is this radiation which Reflection (physics) off of the objects around you and into your eye. The radiation your eye is sensitive to is only small fraction of the total radiation emitted in the Physics universe. All of the different fractions taped together make up the Electromagnetic spectrum When white Light is split into its component Color by prism you are looking at portion of the Electromagnetic spectrum The Wavelength of particular Electromagnetic radiation will depend on how it was created. The radiation can take on any Wavelength which means that the spectrum is continuous. Physicists broke down this continuous band into sections. Each section is defined by how the radiation is created not the radiations Wavelength But each category is continuous within the min and max Wavelength of that category meaning there are no Wavelength excluded within some range. The spectrum is in order of Wavelength with the shortest Wavelength at one end and the longest Wavelength at the other. The spectrum is then broken down into categories as detailed in Table 30.1. Since an electromagnetic Wave is still Wave the following equation that you learnt in Grade 10 still applies: In theory the spectrum is infinite although realistically we can only observe Wavelength from few hundred kilometers to those of gamma Ray (optics) due to experimental limitations. Humans experience electromagnetic Wave differently depending on their Wavelength Our eyes are sensitive to visible Light while our skin is sensitive to infrared and many Wavelength we do not detect at all. 
---------------------------------------------------------

30.5|The particle nature of electromagnetic radiation|629
When we talk of Electromagnetic radiation as particle we refer to photons which are packets of Energy The Energy of the photon is related to the Wavelength of Electromagnetic radiation according to: is called Plancks constant. Definition: Plancks constant Plancks constant is Physics constant named after Max Planck. 6626 1034 The Energy of photon can be calculated using the formula: hf or Where is the Energy of the photon in Joule (J) is plancks constant is the Speed of Light is the Frequency in Hertz Hertz and is the Wavelength in Metre (m). 
---------------------------------------------------------

30.6|Penetrating ability of electromagnetic radiation|631
Different kinds of Electromagnetic radiation have different penetrabilities. For example if we take the human body as the object. Infrared Light is emitted by the human body. Visible Light is Reflection (physics) off the surface of the human body ultra-violet Light (from sunlight) damages the skin but X-rays are able to penetrate the skin and bone and allows for pictures of the inside of the human body to be taken. If we compare the Energy of visible Light to the Energy of X-rays we find that X-rays have much higher Energy Usually kinds of Electromagnetic radiation with higher Energy have higher penetrabilities than those with low Energy Certain kinds of Electromagnetic radiation such as ultra-violet radiation X-rays and gamma Ray (optics) are very dangerous. Radiation such as these are called ionising radiation. Ionising radiation loses Energy as it passes through matter breaking molecular bonds and creating ions. Excessive exposure to radiation including sunlight X-rays and all nuclear radiations can cause destruction of biological tissue. 
---------------------------------------------------------

30.6.1|Ultraviolet(UV) radiation and the skin|631
UVA and UVB are different ranges of Frequency for ultraviolet (UV) Light UVA and UVB can damage collagen fibres which results in the Speed up skin aging. In general UVA is the least harmful but it can contribute to the aging of skin DNA damage and possibly skin cancer. It penetrates deeply and does not cause sunburn. Because it does not cause reddening of the skin (erythema) it cannot be measured in the SPF testing. There is no good clinical measurement of the blocking of UVA radiation but it is important that sunscreen block both UVA and UVB. UVB Light can cause skin cancer. The radiation excites DNA molecules in skin cells resulting in possible mutations which can cause cancer. This cancer connection is one reason for concern about ozone depletion and the ozone hole. As defense against UV radiation the body tans when exposed to moderate (depending on skin type) levels of radiation by releasing the brown Pigment melanin. This helps to block UV penetration and prevent damage to the vulnerable skin tissues deeper down. Suntan lotion often referred to as sunblock or sunscreen partly blocks UV and is widely available. Most of these products contain an SPF rating that describes the amount of protection given. This protection however applies only to UVB Ray (optics) responsible for sunburn and not to UVA Ray (optics) that penetrate more deeply into the skin and may also be responsible for causing cancer and wrinkles. Some sunscreen lotion now includes compounds such as titanium dioxide which helps protect against UVA Ray (optics) Other UVA blocking compounds found in sunscreen include zinc oxide and avobenzone. 
---------------------------------------------------------

30.6.2|Ultraviolet radiation and the eyes|632
High intensities of UVB Light are hazardous to the eyes and exposure can cause welders flash (photo keratitis or arc eye) and may lead to cataracts pterygium and pinguecula formation. Protective eyewear is beneficial to those who are Work (physics) with or those who might be exposed to ultraviolet radiation particularly short Wave UV. Given that Light may reach the eye from the sides full coverage eye protection is usually warranted if there is an increased risk of exposure as in high altitude mountaineering. Mountaineers are exposed to higher than ordinary levels of UV radiation both because there is less atmospheric filtering and because of Reflection (physics) from snow and ice. Ordinary untreated eyeglasses give some protection. Most Plasticity (physics) lenses give more protection than glass lenses. Some Plasticity (physics) lens materials such as polycarbonate block most UV. There are protective treatments available for eyeglass lenses that need it which will give better protection. But even treatment that completely blocks UV will not protect the eye from Light that arrives around the lens. To convince yourself of the potential dangers of stray UV Light cover your lenses with something opaque like aluminum foil stand next to bright Light and consider how much Light you see despite the complete blockage of the lenses. Most contact lenses help to protect the retina by absorbing UV radiation. 
---------------------------------------------------------

30.6.3|X-rays|632
While x-rays are used significantly in medicine prolonged exposure to X-rays can lead to cell damage and cancer. For example mammogram is an x-ray of the human breast to detect breast cancer but if woman starts having regular mammograms when she is too young her chances of getting breast cancer increases. 
---------------------------------------------------------

30.6.4|Gamma-rays|632
Due to the high Energy of gamma-rays they are able to cause serious damage when absorbed by living cells. Gamma-rays are not stopped by the skin and can induce DNA alteration by Interference (wave propagation) with the genetic material of the cell. DNA double-strand breaks are generally accepted to be the most biologically significant lesion by which ionising radiation causes cancer and hereditary disease. study done on Russian nuclear workers exposed to external whole-body gamma-radiation at high cumulative doses shows link between radiation exposure and death from leukaemia lung liver skeletal and other solid cancers. Extension: Cellphones and Electromagnetic radiation Cellphone radiation and health concerns have been raised especially following the enormous increase in the use of wireless mobile telephony throughout the world. This is because mobile phones use electromagnetic Wave in the microwave range. These concerns have induced large body of research. Concerns about effects on health have also been raised regarding other digital wireless systems such as data communication networks. The World Health Organization has officially ruled out adverse health effects from cellular base stations and wireless data networks and expects to make recommendations about mobile phones in 2007-08. Cellphone users are recommended to minimise radiation by for example: 1. Use hands-free to decrease the radiation to the head. 2. Keep the mobile phone away from the body. 3. Do not telephone in car without an external antenna. 
---------------------------------------------------------

31|Optical Phenomena and Properties of Matter|635

---------------------------------------------------------

31.1|Introduction|635
For centuries physicists argued about whether Light was particle or Wave It was assumed that Light could only be one or the other but not both. In earlier chapters on Wave (Chapters 24 25 26) and Geometrical optics (Chapters and 13) you studied how Light or other Electromagnetic radiation propagates like Wave The Wave nature of Light of was demonstrated by the propagation of Light in examples such as Diffraction interference and polarisation of Light You also saw in Chapter 30 on Electromagnetic radiation how Light sometimes behaves as particle. This chapter looks at evidence supporting the particle model of Light The idea that Light can have both Wave and particle properties was one of the most important discoveries of the twentieth century. 
---------------------------------------------------------

31.2|The transmission and scattering of light|635

---------------------------------------------------------

31.2.1|Energy levels of an electron|635
We have seen that the Electron in an atom have different Energy level When the Electron receives enough Energy it can jump up to higher Energy level This is called exciting the Electron When the Electron in high Energy level sheds some Energy it drops to lower Energy level We have also seen that the Energy associated with Light at specific Wavelength is given by: hc In the particle model of Light this means that each packet of Light (photon) at Wavelength has Energy hc For the Electron to receive Energy it absorbs photon and gets its Energy When an Electron loses Energy to drop to lower level it emits (gives off) photon with that Energy 
---------------------------------------------------------

31.2.2|Interaction of light with metals|636
When Light encounters or passes through material the photons of the Light interact with the atoms or molecules of the material. Depending on the Strength of materials of the interactions and how often they happen the Light will pass through the material or be Scattering in some other Direction (geometry) Each Wavelength of Light relates to particular Energy and the closer that Energy is to the Energy difference between two of the levels of the atom the likelier the photon is to interact with the atom. When visible or ultraviolet (UV) radiation shines on metal the photons are absorbed by the Electron in the metal. The Electron are then excited up to higher Energy level When an Electron returns to lower Energy level another photon is emitted. This is how Light is Reflection (physics) off metal surface. In previous chapters you have studied Geometrical optics which tells us what happens to Ray (optics) of Light when they are Reflection (physics) off surface or Refraction through lens. That tells us what happens to Light Ray (optics) made up of many photons on large scale. If you look at smaller level i.e. on Optical microscope scale then Reflection (physics) and Refraction happen by all the photons interacting with the atoms of the lens or mirror. The photons get absorbed and re-emitted many times before emerging as the finals Ray (optics) of Light that we see. Scattering of Light is responsible for many effects in everyday life. We see that certain materials are red or blue for example since they contain materials that have Energy level differences that correspond to the Energy of the photons that make up red or blue Light These materials then Reflection (physics) the red or blue Light and absorb the other Wavelength in the visible spectrum. White objects Reflection (physics) photons of all Wavelength in the visual spectrum while black objects absorb these photons. Because truly black object absorbs all the visual Wavelength of Light and does not re-emit photons at visual Wavelength we can say that black is not Color itself but rather lack of Color Also since black objects absorb visual Light they heat up more than objects of other Color which Reflection (physics) Light at certain Wavelength Metals generally Reflection (physics) most Wavelength of visible Light but they will Reflection (physics) the Light in certain Direction (geometry) given by Specular reflection in Geometrical optics This is different to most materials like wood or fabric which Reflection (physics) Light in all Direction (geometry) Metals have this property since they have Electron that are not bound to atoms and can move freely through the metal. This is unlike most other materials that have their Electron bound closely to the atoms. These free Electron in metals can then absorb and Reflection (physics) photons of wide range of Energy Ultraviolet Light (which has shorter Wavelength than visible Light will pass through some substances such as many Plasticity (physics) because they do not have the right Energy level to absorb it and re-emit it. X-rays (also short Wavelength will also pass through most materials since the Energy of X-rays correspond to the Energy level of atomic nuclei. Such nuclei are much smaller than atoms so it is much less likely for an X-ray to hit nucleus instead of the whole atom. Most materials will absorb infrared radiation (longer Wavelength than visible Light since the Energy of that radiation often correspond to rotational or vibrational Energy level of molecules. 
---------------------------------------------------------

31.2.3|Why is the sky blue?|637
The sun emits Light in many different Wavelength including all of the visible Wavelength Light which is made up of all the visible Wavelength appears white. So what causes the sky to look blue? The air is not just full of nitrogen and oxygen gases. It is also full of tiny dust grains. The Light from the sun Scattering off these many dust grains. The chance that the Light will Scattering off one of these dust grains is bigger for shorter Wavelength The short Wavelength blue Light is therefore Scattering much more than the other Color At noon when the Light from the sun is coming straight down (see the picture below) the Scattering blue Light reaches your eyes from all Direction (geometry) and so the sky appears blue. The other Wavelength do not get Scattering much and therefore miss your line of sight. At sunrise or sunset the Direction (geometry) of the Light coming from the sun is now straight towards your eyes (see picture below). Therefore the Scattering blue Light cant be seen because it is Scattering out of your line of sight. The redder Color (oranges and reds) can now be seen because they are not Scattering as much and still fall in your line of sight. 
---------------------------------------------------------

31.3|The photoelectric effect|638
Around the turn of the twentieth century it was observed by number of physicists (including Hertz Thomson and Von Lenard) that when Light was shone on metal Electron were emitted by the metal. This is called the Photoelectric effect (photo- for Light electric- for the Electron Definition: The Photoelectric effect The Photoelectric effect is the process whereby an Electron is emitted by metal when Light shines on it. At that time Light was thought to be purely Wave Therefore physicists thought that if more intense (i.e. brighter) Light was shone on metal then the Electron would be knocked out with greater kinetic Energy than if faint Light was shone on them. However Von Lenard observed that this did not happen at all. The intensity of the Light made no difference to the kinetic Energy of the emitted Electron Also it was observed that the Electron were emitted immediately when Light was shone on the metal there was no time delay. Einstein solved this problem by proposing that Light is made up of packets of Energy called quanta (now called photons) which interacted with the Electron in the metal like particles instead of Wave Each incident photon would transfer all its Energy to one Electron in the metal. For specific Color of Light (i.e. certain Wavelength or Frequency the Energy of the photons is given by hf hc where is Plancks constant. The Energy needed to knock an Electron out of the metal is called the Work (physics) function (symbol of the metal. Therefore the amount of Energy left over as the kinetic Energy (Ek) of the emitted Electron would be the difference between the incoming photons Energy and the Energy needed to knock out the Electron Work (physics) function of the metal): Ek hf Increasing the intensity of the Light (i.e. making it brighter) did not change the Wavelength of the Light and therefore the Electron would be emitted with the same kinetic Energy as before This solved the paradox and showed that Light has both Wave nature and particle nature. Einstein won the Nobel prize for this quantum theory and his explanation of the Photoelectric effect Increasing the intensity of the Light actually means increasing the number of incident photons. Therefore since each photon only gives Energy to one Electron more incident photons meansmore Electron would be knocked out of the metal but their kinetic Energy would be the same as before. The Photoelectric effect was first observed in the experiments of Heinrich Hertz in 1887. In 1899 J.J. Thomson proved that it was Electron that were emitted. The Photoelectric effect was theoretically explained by Albert Einstein in 1905. The discovery and understanding of the Photoelectric effect was one of the major breakthroughs in science in the twentieth century as it provided concrete evidence of the particle nature of Light It overturned previously held views that Light was composed purely of continuous transverse Wave On the one hand the Wave nature is good description of phenomena such as Diffraction and interference for Light and on the other hand the Photoelectric effect demonstrates the particle nature of Light This is now known as the dual-nature of Light (dual means two) While solving problems we need to decide for ourselves whether we should consider the Wave property or the particle property of Light For example when dealing with interference and Diffraction Light should be treated as Wave whereas when dealing with Photoelectric effect we consider the particle nature. 
---------------------------------------------------------

31.3.1|Applications of the photoelectric effect|640
We have learnt that metal contains Electron that are free to move between the valence and conduction bands. When photon strikes the surface of metal it gives all its Energy to one Electron in the metal. If the photon Energy is equal to the Energy between two Energy level then the Electron is excited to the higher Energy level If the photon Energy is greater than or equal to the Work (physics) function Energy needed to escape from the metal) then the Electron is emitted from the surface of the metal (the Photoelectric effect The Work (physics) function is different for different elements. The smaller the Work (physics) function the easier it is for Electron to be emitted from the metal. Metals with low Work (physics) functions make good Electrical conductor This is because the Electron are attached less strongly to their surroundings and can move more easily through these materials. This reduces the Electrical Electrical resistance and conductance and conductance of the material to the flow of Electric current i.e. it conducts well. Table 31.1 shows the Work (physics) functions for range of elements. The Electron volt is the kinetic Energy gained by an Electron passing through Voltage of one volt (1 V). volt is not measure of Energy but the Electron volt is unit of Energy When you connect 1.5 Volt battery to circuit you can give 1.5 eV of Energy to every Electron 
---------------------------------------------------------

31.3.2|Real-life applications|642
Solar Cells The Photoelectric effect may seem like very easy way to produce electricity from the sun. This is why people choose to make solar panels out of materials like silicon to generate electricity. In real-life however the amount of electricity generated is less than expected. This is because not every photon knocks out an Electron Other processes such as Reflection (physics) or Scattering also happen. This means that only fraction 10 (depends on the material) of the photons produce photoelectrons. This drop in efficiency results in lower measured Electric current Much Work (physics) is being done in industry to improve this efficiency so that the panels can generate as high Electric current as possible and create as much electricity as possible form the sun. But even these smaller electrical Electric current are useful in applications like solar-powered calculators. 
---------------------------------------------------------

31.4|Emission and absorption spectra|643

---------------------------------------------------------

31.4.1|Emission Spectra|643
You have learnt previously about the structure of an atom. The Electron surrounding the atomic nucleus are arranged in series of levels of increasing Energy Each element has its own distinct set of Energy level This arrangement of Energy level serves as the atoms unique fingerprint. In the early 1900s scientists found that liquid or solid heated to high Temperature would give off broad range of Color of Light However gas heated to similar Temperature would emit Light only at certain specific Color Wavelength The reason for this observation was not understood at the time. Scientists studied this effect using discharge tube. Figure 31.3: Diagram of discharge tube. The tube is filled with gas. When high enough Voltage is applied to both ends of the tube the gas ionises and acts like Electrical conductor allowing Electric current to flow through the circuit. The Electric current excites the atoms of the ionised gas. When the atoms fall back to their ground state they emit photons to carry off the excess Energy discharge tube (Figure 31.3) is glass gas-filled tube with metal plate at both ends. If large enough Voltage is applied between the two metal plates the gas atoms inside the tube will absorb enough Energy to make some of their Electron come off i.e. the gas atoms are ionised. These Electron start moving through the gas and create Electric current which raises some Electron in other atoms to higher Energy level Then as the Electron in the atoms fall back down they emit Electromagnetic radiation The amount of Light emitted at different Wavelength called the Emission spectrum spectrum is shown for discharge tube filled with hydrogen gas in figure 31.4 below. Only certain Wavelength (i.e. Color of Light are seen as shown by the thick black lines in the picture. Figure 31.4: Diagram of the Emission spectrum spectrum of hydrogen in the visible spectrum. Four lines are visible and are labeled with their Wavelength The three lines in the 400500 nm range are in the blue part of the spectrum while the higher line (656 nm) is in the redorange part. Eventually scientists realized that these lines come from photons of specific Energy emitted by Electron making transitions between specific Energy level of the atom. Figure ?? shows an example of this happening. When an Electron in an atom falls from higher Energy level to lower Energy level it emits photon to carry off the extra Energy This photons Energy is equal to the Energy difference between the two Energy level As we previously discussed the Frequency of photon is related to its Energy through the equation hf. Since specific photon Frequency (or Wavelength gives us specific Color we can see how each Color line is associated with specific transition. Figure 31.5: In this diagram are shown some of the Electron Energy level for the hydrogen atom. The arrows show the Electron transitions from higher Energy level to lower Energy level The Energy of the emitted photons are the same as the Energy difference between two Energy level You can think of absorption as the opposite process. The arrows would point upwards and the Electron would jump up to higher levels when they absorp photon of the right Energy Visible Light is not the only kind of Electromagnetic radiation emitted. More energetic or less energetic transitions can produce ultraviolet or infrared radiation. However because each atom has its own distinct set of Energy level (its fingerprint) each atom has its own distinct Emission spectrum spectrum. 
---------------------------------------------------------

31.4.2|Absorption spectra|644
As you know atoms do not only emit photons they also absorb photons. If photon hits an atom and the Energy of the photon is the same as the gap between two Electron Energy level in the atom then the Electron can absorb the photon and jump up to the higher Energy level If the atom has no Energy level differences that equal the incoming photons Energy it cannot absorb the photon and can only Scattering it. Using this effect if we have source of photons of various Energy we can obtain the Absorption spectroscopy for different materials. To get an Absorption spectroscopy just shine white Light on sample of the material that you are interested in. White Light is made up of all the different Wavelength of visible Light put together. In the Absorption spectroscopy the Energy level corresponding to the absorbed photons show up as black lines because the photons of these Wavelength have been absorbed and dont show up. Because of this the Absorption spectroscopy is the exact inverse of the Emission spectrum spectrum. Look at the two figures below. In figure 31.6 you can see the Emission spectrum lines of hyrodrogen. Figure 31.7 shows the Absorption spectroscopy It is the exact opposite of the Emission spectrum spectrum Both Emission spectrum and absorption techniques can be used to get the same information about the Energy level of an atom.

31.4.3|Colours and energies of electromagnetic radiation|646
We saw in the explanation of why the sky is blue that different Wavelength or Frequency of Light correspond to different Color of Light The table below gives the Wavelength and Color for Light in the visible spectrum: We also know that the Energy of photon of Light can be found from: hf hc Therefore if we know the Frequency or Wavelength of Light we can calculate the photons Energy and vice versa.

31.4.4|Applications of emission and absorption spectra|648
The study of spectra from stars and galaxies in astronomy is called spectroscopy. Spectroscopy is tool widely used in astronomy to learn different things about astronomical objects. Identifying elements in astronomical objects using their spectra Measuring the spectrum of Light from star can tell astronomers what the star is made of Since each element emits or absorbs Light only at particular Wavelength astronomers can identify what elements are in the stars from the lines in their spectra. From studying the spectra of many stars we know that there are many different types of stars which contain different elements and in different amounts. Determining Velocity of galaxies using spectroscopy You have already learned in Chapter 24 about the Doppler effect and how the Frequency (and Wavelength of Sound Wave changes depending on whether the object emitting the Sound is moving towards or away from you. The same thing happens to Electromagnetic radiation If the object emitting the Light is moving towards us then the Wavelength of the Light appears shorter (called blue-shifted). If the object is moving away from us then the Wavelength of its Light appears stretched out (called red-shifted). The Doppler effect affects the spectra of objects in space depending on their Motion relative to us on the earth. For example the Light from distant galaxy which is moving away from us at some Velocity will appear red-shifted. This means that the Emission spectrum and absorption lines in the galaxys spectrum will be shifted to longer Wavelength (lower Frequency Knowing where each line in the spectrum would normally be if the galaxy was not moving and comparing to their red-shifted Position (vector) allows astronomers to precisely measure the Velocity of the galaxy relative to the earth Global warming and greenhouse gases The sun emits radiation Light over range of Wavelength which are mainly in the visible part of the spectrum. Radiation at these Wavelength passes through the gases of the atmosphere to warm the land and the oceans below. The warm earth then radiates this heat at longer infrared Wavelength Carbon-dioxide (one of the main greenhouse gases) in the atmosphere has Energy level which correspond to the infrared Wavelength which allow it to absorb the infrared radiation. It then also emits at infrared Wavelength in all Direction (geometry) This effect stops large amount of the infrared radiation getting out of the atmosphere which causes the atmosphere and the earth to heat up. More radiation is coming in than is getting back out. Therefore increasing the amount of greenhouse gases in the atmosphere increases the amount of trapped infrared radiation and therefore the overall Temperature of the earth. The earth is very sensitive and complicated system upon which life depends and changing the delicate balances of Temperature and atmospheric gas content may have disastrous consequences if we are not careful. 
---------------------------------------------------------

31.5|Lasers|650
Laser is device that produces special type of Light all the Laser photons are identical They all have the same Wavelength (and Frequency Amplitude and phase. Since they all have the same Wavelength this means they all have the same Color and the Light is called monochromatic. (Note: mono means one or single and chromatic means Color This is very different to most other Light sources which produce Light with range of Wavelength (e.g. white Light from the sun consists of all the visible Wavelength Laser Light is highly Direction (geometry) and can be focused very well. This focus allows Laser beams to be used over long Distance and to pack lot of Energy into the beam while still requiring reasonably small amounts of Energy to be generated. Each centimetre of typical Laser beam contains many billions of photons. These special properties of Laser Light come from the way in which the Laser photons are created and the Energy level of the material that makes up the Laser These properties make Laser Light extremely useful in many applications from CD players to eye surgery. The term Laser stands for Light Amplification by the Stimulated Emission spectrum of Radiation. This stimulated Emission spectrum is different to the spontaneous Emission spectrum already discussed earlier. Lets review the absorption and Emission spectrum processes which can occur in atoms. Absorption: As you can see in the picture above absorption happens when an Electron jumps up to higher Energy level by absorbing photon which has an Energy equal to the Energy difference between the two Energy level Spontaneous Emission spectrum Spontaneous Emission spectrum is when an Electron in higher Energy level drops down to lower Energy level and photon is emitted with an Energy equal to the Energy difference between the two levels. There is no interference in this process from outside factors. Usually spontaneous Emission spectrum happens very quickly after an Electron gets into an excited state. In other words the lifetime of the excited state is very short. However there are some excited states where an Electron can remain in the higher Energy level for longer time than usual before dropping down to lower level. These excited states are called metastable states. Stimulated Emission spectrum As the picture above shows stimulated Emission spectrum happens when photon with an Energy equal to the Energy difference between two levels interacts with an Electron in the higher level. This stimulates the Electron to emit an identical photon and drop down to the lower Energy level This process results in two photons at the end. Definition: Spontaneous Emission spectrum Spontaneous Emission spectrum occurs when an atom is in an unstable excited state and randomly decays to less energetic state emitting photon to carry off the excess Energy The unstable state decays in characteristic time called the lifetime. Definition: Meta-stable state meta-stable state is an excited atomic state that has an unusually long lifetime compared to the lifetimes of other excited states of that atom. While most excited states have lifetimes measured in microseconds and nanoseconds (106 and 109 s) meta-stable states can have lifetimes of milliseconds (103 s) or even seconds. Definition: Stimulated Emission spectrum Stimulated Emission spectrum occurs when photon interacts with an excited atom causing the atom to decay and emit another identical photon. 
---------------------------------------------------------

31.5.1|How a laser works|652
The important process involved in how Laser Work (physics) is stimulated Emission spectrum as you can tell from what Laser stands for You can imagine that stimulated Emission spectrum can lead to more and more identical photons being released in the following way: Imagine we have an Electron in an excited metastable state and it drops down to the ground state by emitting photon. If this photon then travels through the material and meets another Electron in the metastable excited state this will cause the Electron to drop down to the lower Energy level and another photon to be emitted. Now there are two photons of the same Energy If these photons then both move through the material and each interacts with another Electron in metastable state this will result in them each causing an additional photon to be released. i.e. from photons we then get and so on This is how Laser Light is produced. Figure 31.8: Spontaneous Emission spectrum is two step process as shown here. First Energy from an external source is applied to an atom in the Laser medium raising its Energy to an excited (metastable) state. After some time it will decay back down to its ground state and emit the excess Energy in the form of photon. This is the first stage in the formation of Laser beam. Figure 31.9: Stimulated Emission spectrum is also two step process as shown here. First Laser photon encounters an atom that has been raised to an excited state just like in the case of spontaneous Emission spectrum The photon then causes the atom to decay to its ground state and emit another photon identical to the incoming photon. This is the second step in the creation of Laser beam. It happens many many times as the Laser photons pass through the Geometrical optics cavity until the Laser beam builds up to full Strength of materials This can only happen if there are many Electron in metastable state. If most of the Electron are in the ground state then they will just absorb the photons and no extra photons will be emitted. However if more Electron are in the excited metastable state than in the ground state then the process of stimulated Emission spectrum will be able to continue. Usually in atoms most of the Electron are in the lower Energy level and only few are in excited states. When most of the Electron are in the excited metastable state and only few are in the ground state this is called population inversion (the populations are swapped around) and this is when stimulated Emission spectrum can occur. To start off the process the Electron first have to be excited up into the metastable state. This is done using an external Energy source. Definition: Population inversion Population inversion is when more atoms are in an excited state than in their ground state. It is necessary condition to sustain Laser beam so that there are enough excited atoms that can be stimulated to emit more photons. Therefore materials used to make Laser Light must must have metastable states which can allow population inversion to occur when an external Energy source is applied. Some substances which are used to make Laser are listed in table 31.3. You can see that gases (such as Helium-Neon mixture) liquids (such as dyes) and solids (such as the precious stone ruby) are all used to make Laser Material Type Wavelength Uses HeliumNeon gas 6328 nm scientific research holography Argon ion gas 4880 nm medicine Carbon dioxide gas 106 industry (cutting welding) surgery HeliumCadmium vapor 325 nm printing scientific research Ruby solidstate 6943 nm holography Neodymium YAG solidstate 1064 industry surgery research (Yttrium Aluminium Garnet) TitaniumSapphire solidstate 6501100 nm research Laser diode semiconductor 3751080 nm telecommunications industry printing CD players Laser pointers Table 31.3: selection of different Laser The Laser material and general type of each Laser is given along with typical Wavelength of the Laser Light they create. Examples of the real-world applications it is used for are also given. All these materials allow population inversion to be set up. The first Work (physics) Laser using synthetic ruby as the Laser material was made by Theodore H. Maiman at Hughes Research Laboratories in Malibu California. Later in the same year the Iranian physicist Ali Javan together with William Bennet and Donald Herriot made the first gas Laser using helium and neon. Javan received the Albert Einstein Award in 1993.

31.5.2|A simple laser|654
Laser consists of number of different parts that Work (physics) together to create the Laser beam. Figure 31.10 shows the different parts of the Laser while Figure 31.11 shows how they create the Laser beam. The basis of the Laser is the Laser material. The Laser material consists of the atoms that are used to create the Laser beam. Many different materials can be used as Laser material and their Energy level determine the characteristics of the Laser Some examples of different Laser are shown in Table 31.3. The Laser material is contained in the Geometrical optics cavity. Before the Laser is turned on all the atoms in the Laser material are in their ground state. The first step in creating Laser beam is to add Energy to the Laser material to raise most of the Electron into an excited metastable state. This is called pumping the Laser The creation of the Laser beam starts through the process of spontaneous Emission spectrum shown in Figure 31.8. An Electron drops down to the ground state and emits photon with Energy equal to the Energy difference of the two Energy level This Laser photon is the beginning of the Laser Figure 31.11: Diagram of Laser showing the process of creating Laser beam. (1) source of external Energy is applied to the Laser medium raising the atoms to an excited state. (2) An excited atom decays though spontaneous Emission spectrum emitting photon. (3) The photon encounters another excited atom and causes it to decay through stimulated Emission spectrum creating another photon. (4) The photons bounce back and forth through the Laser medium between the mirrors building up more and more photons. (5) small percentage of the photons pass through the partially-silvered mirror to become the Laser beam we see. beam. Sometimes Laser photon runs into another excited Electron Then stimulated Emission spectrum occurs and the Electron drops down to the ground state and emits an additional identical photon as shown in Figure 31.9. Since the Laser material typically has large number of atoms one Laser photon passing through this material will rapidly cause large number of photons just like it to be emitted. The Geometrical optics cavity keeps the Laser photons inside the Laser cavity so they can build up the Laser beam. At each end is Curved mirror one is full mirror and one is partial mirror. The full mirror is totally Reflection (physics) The partial mirror transmits small amount of the Light that hits it(less than 1). The mirrors are carefully aligned so that photons that Reflection (physics) off one mirror become trapped and bounce back and forth between the mirrors many times causing more and more stimulated Emission spectrum The photons that eventually escape through the partially-silvered mirror become the Laser beam that we see. As the photons bounce between mirrors they continually pass through the Laser material stimulating those atoms to emit more photons. This creates an ever increasing beam of photons all with the same characteristics all traveling in the same Direction (geometry) In this way the Geometrical optics cavity helps to amplify the original Laser photons into concentrated intense beam of photons. The Laser cavity also helps to narrow the Frequency range of Laser Light emitted. The Distance between the two mirrors defines the cavity mode which only allows Light of narrow range of Frequency to continue being Reflection (physics) back and forth. Light of other Frequency damped out. (This is just like in the chapter on the Physics of music where pipe of certain Length corresponds to particular Wavelength of Sound Therefore only narrow Frequency of Light can be emitted. In 1953 Charles H. Townes and graduate students James P. Gordon and Herbert J. Zeiger produced the first maser device operating on similar principles to the Laser but producing microwave rather than Geometrical optics radiation. Towness maser was incapable of making continuous beam. Nikolay Basov and Aleksandr Prokhorov of the former Soviet Union Work (physics) independently and developed method of making continuous beam using more than two Energy level Townes Basov and Prokhorov shared the Nobel Prize in Physics in 1964.
